PUBLIC COMMENT
During the public comment period, members of the public may speak on general items of interest within the Commission's
jurisdiction that are not on the agenda.  Each member of the public may speak for a maximum of three minutes with a maximum of
15 minutes for the entire public comment period. The Chair shall determine whether the matter is within the Commission's
jurisdiction. The Commission shall not act on or discuss any matters raised during the public comment period, which are not on the
agenda, but shall refer such matters to staff for review and/or request such matters be placed on a future agenda.
PUBLIC HEARING
Planning Commission decisions are final unless appealed to the City Council in accordance with Section 27.08.090 and Section
27.08.060 of the San Mateo Municipal Code. The time within which judicial review of any final decision may be sought is governed by
Code of Civil Procedure section 1094.6. If any person challenges a Planning action in court, they may be limited to raising only those
issues raised at the public hearing or in written correspondence delivered to the City of San Mateo, at or prior to, the public hearing.
Some public hearings will be automatically referred to City Council and those will be indicated below.
 
1.
715 N. San Mateo Drive – New Multifamily Residential Development (PA-2025-031)
Adopt a Resolution approving a Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR), a Site Development Planning
Application (SDPA), and a Vesting Tentative Parcel Map (VTM) for the construction of a new multifamily
residential building with 181 dwelling units and associated site improvements at 715 N. San Mateo Drive, and
find that the Project is exempt from further review under the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA)
pursuant to Public Resources Code section 21080.66, based on the Findings for Approval and subject to the
Conditions of Approval.

--- page 2 ---
CEQA: Approval of the Project is subject to a statutory exemption under Public Resources Code section 21080.66,
signed into law by AB 130. To facilitate the City’s review of the Project under this exemption, on August 11, 2025, the
applicant provided a memo to detail the Project’s qualification under Public Resources Code section 21080.66(a)
(Attachment 6). An assessment the Project complies with AB 130 is in the attached Draft Resolution.
In accordance with Public Resources Code section 21080.66(b)(1)(A), the City formally noticed Native American
tribes for consultation regarding the Project and its potential impacts on tribal cultural resources. One tribe
responded to the City’s notice to request consultation with the City. The Project Conditions of Approval (Attachment
1, Exhibit A) include conditions required to satisfy the requirements of AB 130 to avoid impacts on tribal cultural
resources.

SUBJECT: 
715 N. San Mateo Drive – New Multifamily Residential Development (PA-2025-031) 
 
RECOMMENDATION 
Adopt a Resolution approving a Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR), a Site Development Planning Application (SDPA), 
and a Vesting Tentative Parcel Map (VTM) for the construction of a new multifamily residential building with 181 dwelling 
units and associated site improvements at 715 N. San Mateo Drive, and find that the Project is exempt from further review 
under the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant to Public Resources Code section 21080.66, based on the 
Findings for Approval and subject to the Conditions of Approval. 
 
BACKGROUND: 
On April 15, 2025, Prometheus Real Estate Group (applicant) submitted a Planning Application to demolish two one-story 
commercial buildings and one two-story duplex to construct a six-story multifamily residential building (“Project”) consisting 
of 181 dwelling units, parking, and open space. The dwellings would be rented, and 19 would be designated as Below Market 
Rate (BMR) units at the Very-Low Income (VLI) affordability level. 
 
This application follows the submittal of a Preliminary Application (PA-2024-064) made under the Housing Crisis Act (Senate 
Bill 330) on November 14, 2024. The Project’s Neighborhood Meeting was held on February 26, 2025, ahead of the formal 
submittal (more details below).  
 
Project Site 
The Project site is located west of North San Mateo Drive, with State Street on the northwest and Villa Terrace on the 
southeast, is comprised of four parcels, and is approximately 1.22 acres, or 53,141 square feet, in size. The existing site 
includes approximately 5,330 square feet of commercial floor area within two one-story buildings with surface parking along 
North San Mateo Drive, that is currently used for as parking for the vehicle maintenance business across the street, and one 
1,960-square-foot, two-story residential duplex at 247 Villa Terrace (unit 1 is registered with the City as a short-term rental 
and unit 2 is occupied by a long-term tenant). Surrounding uses include single-family and multifamily residences to the 
southeast and southwest, auto-related businesses to the northeast, and a fitness business to the northwest. To the north 
and opposite the site across the street is the 888 San Mateo Apartments, a three-story multifamily development completed 
in 2014. 
 
The Project site, and the properties abutting North San Mateo Drive to the north and south of the site, are within the General 
Plan Land Use designation of Residential Medium II. The Project site, and the properties along North San Mateo Drive to the 
north and south, are also within one of the ten General Plan 2040 study areas, where the City increased allowable building 
height, density, and FAR. The Project site and vicinity are not within a Specific Plan, Master Plan, or Area Plan boundary. The 
Project site is zoned “Regional/Community Commercial District” (C3-2) and “Executive Offices District” (E2-1.5), and the 
Burlingame Caltrain stop is less than one-half mile north of the site. A location map showing the Project site is included as 
Attachment 2.

--- page 4 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO 
 
 
 
 
Project Description 
The Project includes construction of a six-story, 258,018-square-foot multifamily residential building with 181 residential 
units and 180 off-street covered parking spaces. The ground floor includes 14 dwellings (ten along North San Mateo Drive 
and four along Villa Terrace), the 2nd and 6th floors contain 31 dwellings per floor, and the 3rd, 4th, and 5th floors contain 35 
dwellings per floor. The Below Market Rate (BMR) dwellings will be distributed throughout each floor and each story of the 
proposed building. The dwelling mix is shown in Table 1 below.

Primary pedestrian access would be provided along North San Mateo Drive, with secondary access provided on State Street 
and Villa Terrace. Parking would be provided in a two-level parking garage, with 131 stalls below grade and 49 on the ground 
floor, accessed via a new driveway and curb cut to Villa Terrace. Bicycle parking facilities would include secure racks within 
a 196-space bike-parking room at grade, located adjacent to the residential lobby, and exterior bike racks to accommodate 
12 short-term bicycle parking spaces, located in the public right-of-way adjacent to the residential lobby along North San 
Mateo Drive. Residential amenities would be provided, to include a mail/package room, lobby, coworking space and dog 
washing area on the ground floor, a gym/fitness room, a pool/spa and courtyard on the 2nd floor, and a common room and 
amenity deck with a barbeque area on the 6th floor (overall, approximately 27,000 square feet of open space would be 
provided). Within the public right-of-way fronting the site, the Project would remove six curb cuts/driveways and all 
curbs/sidewalks to install new sidewalks with pedestrian-scaled lighting, landscape planters with street trees, and new bulb-
outs and ADA curb ramps at the intersection of San Mateo Drive and State Street and at San Mateo Drive and Villa Terrace. 
Architectural, Landscape, and Civil plans are included in Attachment 3. 
 
APPLICABLE CODE AND POLICY REVIEW: 
General Plan and Zoning Code 
The General Plan 2040 Land Use Designation for the Project site is Residential Medium II, which allows medium-density 
multifamily residential dwellings, such as condominiums and apartments, near mixed-use, office, and/or commercial areas.  
The Residential Medium II designation allows for residential densities of up to 99 dwellings per acre, and for this 1.22-acre 
site, the base density allows a maximum of 121 dwellings. To achieve 181 dwellings, the applicant requested a density bonus 
under State law, which is further discussed below. A discussion of the General Plan policies is included in the Draft Resolution 
(Attachment 1). 
 
The Project site is zoned “Regional/Community Commercial District” (C3-2) and “Executive Offices District” (E2-1.5), and 
development of this site is subject to development standards outlined in San Mateo Municipal Code (“SMMC”) Chapters 
27.34 and 27.48. A Project Data Table listing the applicable Zoning Code standards and the Project’s conformance to them 
is included as Attachment 4.  
 
Automobile Parking Standards 
The Project site is located within one-half mile of the Downtown Burlingame Caltrain Stop, which is considered a major 
transit stop as defined in Public Resources Code section 21155, and per Government Code section 65863.2 (approved under 
Assembly Bill (AB) 2097). Based on these state statutes, the City is prohibited from imposing any minimum automobile 
parking requirements on the Project. Therefore, the parking requirements in the City’s Zoning Code do not apply, and the 
City cannot require any off-street parking. Nonetheless, the Project is providing 180 off-street parking spaces to 
 
1 “Urban 1-bed” is a type of studio dwelling, with a partial wall separating the living and sleeping areas. Since the separation is not a full wall, the sleeping area is not 
counted as a bedroom, and an urban 1-bed is considered a studio dwelling for the purpose of confirming automobile and bicycle parking.

--- page 5 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO 
 
 
 
 
accommodate the expected demand for residential parking. In addition, the Project would implement Transportation 
Demand Management (TDM) measures through the C/CAG checklist. 
 
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) 
The Project requires a Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) approval for construction of a new building in accordance 
with SMMC section 27.08.030. The Project is consistent with the required SPAR findings: it proposes a multifamily 
development that complements the existing architectural character of the surrounding neighborhood through the use of 
high-quality materials and extensive landscaping, which enhances the overall visual character of the site and adjacent area. 
The Project will support the harmonious and orderly growth of the City, the desirability of investment and occupation in the 
vicinity, and be in the best interests of the public health, safety, or welfare. Overall, the Project design supports orderly and 
harmonious development of the site, complies with applicable development standards and General Plan policies, and would 
not result in adverse impacts. Details on the SPAR findings for approval are included in the Draft Resolution (Attachment 1). 
 
Site Development Planning Application (SDPA) 
The Project also requires a Site Development Planning Application (SDPA) approval for the removal of major vegetation and 
protected trees on and adjacent to the site in accordance with SMMC section 23.40.030. The SMMC defines “major 
vegetation” as live vegetation consisting of tree growth with a trunk diameter of six inches or greater measured at 54 inches 
above natural grade, and “protected trees” as any oak tree with a minimum diameter of 10 inches measured at 54 inches 
above natural grade, any tree with a diameter of 15 inches measured at 54 inches above natural grade, or any street tree. 
 
The Project will result in the removal of 19 existing trees, of which four are protected. The removal of 17 trees on-site is 
necessary to facilitate the development of the Project, and the removal of two trees within the public right-of-way would 
remove trees deemed by the Arborist to be unsuitable in their existing locations. Fifty-five trees will be planted on-site on 
the 2nd and 6th floors of the Project, and 25 trees will be planted along all project frontages in the public right-of-way. The 
equivalent landscape unit (LU) value of the removed trees will be replaced, as conditioned, through the planting of new 
trees, payment of an in-lieu fee, or a combination of both, in accordance with SMMC Chapter 27.71. Details regarding the 
SDPA findings for approval are provided in the Draft Resolution (Attachment 1). 
 
APPLICABLE HOUSING LAWS: 
State Density Bonus Law 
The Project utilizes the provisions of State Density Bonus Law in accordance with Government Code section 65915 and as 
locally adopted in SMMC Chapter 27.15, Density Bonus. To comply with Density Bonus regulations, the City must allow for 
increased residential density, “concessions,” and “waivers” from development standards for residential projects that provide 
a certain percentage of units as affordable units. 
 
The Project proposes 181 dwelling units, exceeding the Residential Medium II land use designation maximum density 
established by the San Mateo General Plan 2040. The Project, however, would designate 15% of the base density units as 
BMR units at the Very Low-Income (VLI) affordability level. Per Government Code section 65915(f)(2), a project with at least 
15% of the dwellings designated as affordable for VLI households is eligible for a density bonus of 50% of the base density. 
This density bonus would increase the maximum allowable density up to 182 dwellings2. Therefore, the density proposed by 
the Project is consistent with the General Plan and state law.  
 
Concession and Waiver Requests 
For this Project, State Density Bonus Law also allows the applicant to request up to three concessions, per Government Code 
section 65915(d)(2)(C), and unlimited waivers from development standards, per Government Code section 65915(e). 
Generally speaking, a concession (or incentive) is a reduction or modification of a development standard that results in 
identifiable and actual cost reductions to provide for affordable housing costs, helping to make the Project financially 
feasible. (A concession also includes a reduction in site development standards or a modification of zoning code 
requirements that exceed minimum building standards.) A waiver is a modification of a standard that would otherwise 
 
2 The General Plan density for this site is 120.7 dwellings, and per Government Code section 65915(q), the density is rounded up to 121 dwellings. The 50% bonus, when 
applied to this density, would allow 181.5 dwellings, and per Government Code section 65915(q), the total number of dwellings allowed for this site is rounded up to 182 
dwellings.

physically preclude the construction of the Project at the allowed density. The Project application does not identify any 
concession requests under State Density Bonus Law. However, the Project is seeking several waivers for aspects of the 
Project that do not meet various City development standards, such as floor area ratio (FAR), setbacks/yards, landscape 
buffers, and open space3. The applicant provided a summary of the Project waivers in a density bonus request letter 
(Attachment 5). A complete list of the Project waivers is included in Attachment 1, Exhibit B. 
 
Staff evaluated the waivers and concluded that the waivers are consistent with State law requirements because they support 
construction of the Project as it is designed and at the densities permitted under the City’s General Plan and State Density 
Bonus Law.  
 
Other Applicable State Laws 
In addition to State Density Bonus Law, there are several other state laws that regulate housing development projects. For 
this Project, these include, but are not necessarily limited to the following: 
• 
The Housing Crisis Act (Senate Bill 330) 
o Under Senate Bill 330 (SB 330), a project vests the ordinances, policies, and standards adopted and in effect 
when a preliminary application was submitted to the City. This Project submitted a Preliminary Application 
under SB 330 on November 14, 2024, and is therefore subject to the ordinances, policies, and standards in 
place as of that date.  
• 
The Housing Accountability Act (HAA)  
o The HAA limits a local agency’s ability to deny, reduce the density of, or render housing development 
projects infeasible if objective standards are met. Additionally, when a Project receives waivers from 
objective standards under State Density Bonus Law, it is still considered in compliance with those objective 
standards for the purpose of the HAA. As proposed, including the allowed waivers, this Project meets all 
applicable objective standards in the General Plan, Zoning Code, and other local policy documents that were 
in effect at the time the preliminary application was submitted under SB330. 
• 
Assembly Bill 130 
o Assembly Bill 130 (AB 130) mandates an expedited review timeline and a statutory exemption under CEQA 
for housing projects meeting certain criteria. As discussed below, and in detail in the attached Resolution, 
the Project meets criteria and is subject to expedited review and a statutory exemption under CEQA.  
 
Inclusionary Housing Requirements 
The City’s Below Market Rate (Inclusionary) Program requires rental projects of 11 or more dwellings to reserve at least 15 
percent of the dwellings for lower-income households. The applicant proposes to reserve 19 dwellings, or 15.7 percent of 
the site’s base density (99 units/acre), for VLI households, which exceeds the City’s Inclusionary Program requirements. 
Consistent with the City’s Policy, the VLI dwellings are distributed throughout the development and, like the market-rate 
dwellings, have access to all on-site amenities, are generally comparable in size, and share the same exterior design and 
appearance. 
 
DESIGN REVIEW – OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS: 
The Project was reviewed for consistency with the City’s Multifamily and Residential Mixed-Use Objective Design Standards 
(ODS). The proposed architectural style is best characterized as contemporary, expressed through a combination of white 
and gray stucco with wood-appearance siding and brick accents that define building form. 
 
The Project design presents a clear base, middle, and top, and each building corner (at State Street and Villa Terrace) is 
defined with brick cladding and building recesses at each floor to provide private open space for the adjacent dwelling. 
Overall, the building combines four primary materials (wall material to include brick, stucco, faux wood siding, and steel for 
railings) and four colors (white and gray stucco, tan and black brick cladding, ‘Golden Oak’ wood appearance siding, and 
black for railings, doors, and windows). The pedestrian experience along each street frontage is enhanced with landscape 
planters and trees along the curb and regular building entries, windows, and pedestrian-scale lighting to provide a sense of 
 
3 Within the applicant’s density bonus request letter, “Building height” is listed as a waiver or reduction. However, with the adoption of Measure T, the General Plan 2040 
Land Use Designation for this site permits building height of up to 6 stories. As the Project would include only 6 stories, the Project complies with the City’s height limit, and 
this waiver is not needed.

security along the building frontage and sidewalk.  
 
The Project is consistent with the City’s ODS, except for ODS section 4.1.1, where the ground floor wall facing the residential 
district to the southwest is defined as a “Blank Wall” because it would exceed the height and length maximum allowed 
without also providing a window or door. While the applicant proposed architectural detailing and trailing vines to improve 
the appearance of this wall, the ground-floor wall does not comply, and the applicant has requested a waiver pursuant to 
State Density Bonus Law. 
 
TRANSPORTATION ANALYSIS: 
General Plan 2040 Circulation Element Policy C 6.3 requires a site-specific transportation impact analysis prepared in 
accordance with the City’s adopted Transportation Impact Analysis (TIA) Policy for development projects that may result in 
an adverse condition or effect on the roadway system. This is a local policy requirement and is independent of CEQA VMT 
analysis.4 A Local Transportation Analysis (LTA) was prepared by the applicant’s consultant, Hexagon, to demonstrate 
compliance with this General Plan Policy and the City’s TIA Guidelines. The trip generation analysis indicates that the Project 
would generate a gross of 807 average daily trips, with 69 trips (16 inbound and 53 outbound) during the AM peak hour and 
69 trips (44 inbound and 25 outbound) during the PM peak hour. 
 
Hexagon performed a Level of Service (LOS) Analysis at three nearby intersections for this Project to find that it would 
operate at an acceptable LOS with and without the addition of project trips under all evaluated scenarios5. The Hexagon 
Local Transportation Analysis (LTA) is included as Attachment 7. Overall, the LTA found that the Project would not result in 
any significant local traffic or circulation impacts. 
 
Vesting Tentative Parcel Map 
In addition to the SPAR application, the Project would also merge the four existing parcels into one parcel, and this merger 
would be accomplished via a Parcel Map. Per SMMC section 26.56.075, when a Tentative Parcel Map is accompanied by a 
planning application, it is subject to review and action by the Planning Commission. Findings to approve the Parcel Map are 
included in the attached Draft Resolution, and the conditions of approval include a condition to require that the final map 
to merge the parcels be filed prior to issuance of a building permit for the new building.  
 
NOTICE PROVIDED: 
In accordance with Government Code section 65090, notice of this public hearing was published in the San Mateo Daily 
Journal ten days in advance of this Planning Commission meeting. In accordance with Government Code section 65091 and 
the City’s Municipal Code noticing requirements, notice was also provided more than ten days in advance of this Planning 
Commission meeting to: 
 
• 
Property owners, residential tenants, and business tenants within 1,000 feet of the Project site. 
• 
The City’s Planning “Notify Me” email list; and 
• 
The interested parties email list, which includes interested individuals who contacted the City and requested to be 
added to the Project notification list. 
 
PUBLIC COMMENTS: 
The applicant held a formal Neighborhood Informational Meeting on February 26, 2025, which was attended by 
approximately 40 participants. A Planner from the City attended as an observer. The discussion and comments at this 
meeting included clarifying questions about the Project, which were answered by the developer, as well as public comments 
focused on concerns about parking adequacy, traffic and construction impacts, and the size of the building (the applicant 
provided meeting notes for this meeting). During the formal application review, no additional public comments were 
submitted to staff. Any public comments received after the publication of this report will be forwarded to the Planning 
Commission for review and consideration and posted to this item on the City’s Agendas & Minutes Public Meeting Portal as 
“Post Packet Public Comments.”

FISCAL IMPACT: 
As a new housing project filed under SB 330, the Project is subject to development impact, in-lieu, and linkage fees in effect 
at the time of the application filing date. Based on the City's Development Fees, the estimated6 fees are listed below (and 
these fees are assessed and collected prior to the issuance of building permits or occupancy): 
 
• 
Wastewater Capacity Charge of approximately $1,26 million to recover a proportionate share of costs for existing 
and future wastewater system facilities and assets from new or expanded connections to City wastewater systems. 
• 
Transportation Improvement Fee of approximately $506,100 to fund citywide traffic improvements. 
• 
Park In-Lieu/Impact Fee of approximately $3.57 million to offset the increased demands on park and recreation 
facilities serving new developments. 
• 
Art in Public Places Fee in the amount of 1.19% of the total building valuation (excluding land acquisition and off-
site improvement cost) in lieu of providing on-site public art. 
• 
Tree Replacement & Landscape In-Lieu Fee of approximately $8,400, which is assessed when a project removes 
more trees than are planted on-site or along street frontages by the project. 
• 
Childcare Development Fee of approximately $601,800 to fund the development of childcare facilities. 
• 
School Impact Fees in the amount of $4.94 per square foot of residential area to offset the increased demands on 
school facilities caused by new development. This is collected by the San Mateo Union High School District for all 
schools in San Mateo. 
 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION: 
Approval of the Project is subject to a new statutory exemption under Public Resources Code section 21080.66, signed into 
law by AB 130. To facilitate the City’s review of the Project under this exemption, on August 11, 2025, the applicant provided 
a memo to detail the Project’s qualification under Public Resources Code section 21080.66(a) (Attachment 6). An assessment 
of how the Project complies with AB 130 is in the attached Draft Resolution.  
 
In accordance with Public Resources Code section 21080.66(b)(1)(A), the City formally noticed Native American tribes for 
consultation regarding the Project and its potential impacts on tribal cultural resources. One tribe responded to the City’s 
notice to request consultation with the City. The Project Conditions of Approval (Attachment 1, Exhibit A) include conditions 
required to satisfy the requirements of AB 130 to avoid impacts on tribal cultural resources.

RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2026)
A RESOLUTION OF THE PLANNING COMMISSION APPROVING SITE PLAN AND ARCHITECTURAL REVIEW, A SITE 
DEVELOPMENT PLANNING APPLICATION (SDPA), AND A VESTING TENTATIVE MAP TO CONSTRUCT 181 
RESIDENTIAL UNITS AND ASSOCIATED SITE IMPROVEMENTS, AND DETERMINE THAT THE PROJECT IS EXEMPT 
FROM FURTHER ENVIRONMENTAL REVIEW UNDER CALIFORNIA ENVIRONMENTAL QUALITY ACT
WHEREAS, Prometheus Real Estate Group (herein referred to as the “Applicant”) submitted a Planning 
Application, No. PA-2025-031, for Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR), a Site Development Planning 
Application (SDPA), and a Vesting Tentative Parcel Map (VTM) to construct a multifamily development with 181 
dwellings and associated off-street parking, landscaping and open space at 715, 723 & 733 North San Mateo Drive 
& 247 Villa Terrace (collectively referred to as “Project”) in the City of San Mateo (“City”); and
WHEREAS, the site of the proposed Project is designated by the General Plan Land Use Plan as Residential 
Medium II and by the Zoning Ordinance as “Regional/Community Commercial District” (C3-2) and “Executive 
Offices District” (E2-1.5); and
WHEREAS, in fulfillment of the City’s Below Market Rate requirement found in San Mateo Municipal Code 
(SMMC) section 27.16.050, the Project would provide 19 dwellings affordable to Very-Low Income (VLI) 
households, to consist of one studio, four “urban one-bedroom”, eight one-bedroom, and six two-bedroom 
dwellings; and
WHEREAS, the Project would reserve at least 15% of the maximum density allowed for this site for VLI 
households, and is eligible for: 1) a density bonus of 50% of the base density (per Government Code section 
65915(f)(2)), 2) three concessions (per Government Code section 65915(d)(2)(C)), and 3) unlimited waivers or 
reductions of development standards (per Government Code section 65915(e)). A list of Project waivers is 
included as Exhibit B, and while the Project is eligible for three concessions, a concession or incentive request was 
not made; and
WHEREAS, the Project is exempt from CEQA under Public Resources Code section 21080.66(a), based on 
findings herein; and
WHEREAS, based on findings herein, and notwithstanding the residential density and the waivers of 
development standards granted under State Density Bonus Law, the Project is consistent with applicable policies 
of the General Plan 2040, the San Mateo Municipal Code, and the City’s Objective Design Standards; and
WHEREAS, SMMC section 27.06.050 requires City Council action on Site Plan and Architectural Review for 
any building that would exceed the height limit in the General Plan, and the Project, at six stories, is within the 
height limit set by the San Mateo General Plan 2040 Land Use Designation of Residential Medium II, which allows 
a building of up to six stories; and
WHEREAS, the Planning Commission held a duly noticed public hearing for the Project on March 24, 2026, 
at which all public comments were considered.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE PLANNING COMMISSION OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY 
FINDS AND RESOLVES that:
1.
The Planning Commission finds, based on the whole record before it, that the Project will not have 
a significant effect on the environment, and that Project approval is exempt from further review

--- page 10 ---
under CEQA, per Public Resources Code section 21080.66, because the Project meets all of the following 
conditions listed in Public Resources Code section 21080.66(a):
a.
The site, at 1.22 acres, is less than 20 acres in size;
b.
The site is located within the City of San Mateo;
c.
The site is developed with urban uses: retail car sales and housing, and is surrounded by 
commercial and residential uses; 
d.
The Project is consistent with the General Plan and zoning ordinance; notwithstanding the 
residential density and waivers of development standards granted under State Density Bonus 
Law;
e.
The residential density would result in a density of 148.3 dwelling units per acre, a density 
that is at least one-half of (and is, in fact, greater than) the density threshold set by 
Government Code section 65583.2(c)(3)(B);
f.
The site is not located within: 1) a coastal zone, 2) prime farmland or farmland of statewide 
importance and is not zoned or designated for agricultural protection or preservation, 3) 
wetlands, 4) a very high fire hazard severity zone, 5) a hazardous waste site, 6) a delineated 
earthquake fault zone, 7) a special flood hazard area, 8) a regulatory floodway, 9) lands 
identified for conservation in an adopted natural community conservation plan, habitat 
conservation plan, or other adopted natural resource protection plan, 10) habitat for 
protected species identified as candidate, sensitive, or species of special status by state or 
federal agencies, fully protected species, or species protected by the federal Endangered 
Species Act of 1973, the California Endangered Species Act, or the Native Plant Protection Act, 
or 11) lands under a conservation easement;
g.
The site does not contain any historic structure(s) listed on a national, state, or local register; 
h.
No portion of the new development would be used as a hotel, motel, bed and breakfast inn, 
or provide other transient lodging; and
i.
The Project is not located within 500 feet of a freeway.
In addition, the Project completed tribal consultation pursuant to Public Resources Code section 
21080.66(b)(1), with one tribe participating in the consultation process. Appropriate conditions 
are included in the Conditions of Approval to avoid significant impacts to tribal cultural resources.
2.
The Site Plan and Architectural Review, the Site Development Planning Application, and the 
Vesting Tentative Parcel Map to construct 181 residential units with associated parking, 
landscaping, open space, and related improvements within the public right-of-way, is approved.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, BY THE PLANNING COMMISSION OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, AS 
FOLLOWS:
General Plan Conformance
1.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Land Use Element.
a.
Policy LU 1.1 Equitable Development. Prioritize development projects that meet social and 
economic needs of the economically vulnerable populations to address and reverse the 
underlying socioeconomic factors in the community that contribute to residential and social 
segregation in the city. Provide a range of housing types, sizes, and affordability levels in all 
San Mateo neighborhoods. 
b.
Policy LU 1.3 Optimize Development Opportunities. Encourage new development in major 
commercial and transit-oriented development areas, including the Downtown, Caltrain 
station areas, and the El Camino Real corridor, to maximize the density and intensity specified 
in the Land Use Plan and to efficiently use land and infrastructure resources.

--- page 11 ---
c.
Policy LU 3.1 Housing Diversity. Promote safe, attractive, and walkable residential 
neighborhoods with diverse types and sizes of homes for individuals, families, and households 
of all income levels.
The Project supports equitable development by providing a diverse mix of dwellings, including 
studio, one-, two-, and three-bedrooms, including 162 market-rate dwellings and 19 dwellings 
reserved for VLI households, within one-half mile of the Downtown Burlingame Caltrain Station. 
The Project optimizes development opportunities by replacing an underutilized commercial 
property and one residential duplex with high-quality residential development that incorporates 
on-site amenities and open spaces. The Project supports housing diversity by offering a range of 
dwelling sizes (from 533 to 1,500 square feet) and bedroom configurations (studio, one-, two-, 
and three-bedroom units).
2.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Circulation Element.
a.
Policy C 3.2 Pedestrian Enhancements with New Development. Require new development 
projects to provide sidewalks and pedestrian ramps and to repair or replace damaged 
sidewalks, in addition to right-of-way improvements identified in adopted City master plans. 
Encourage new developments to include pedestrian-oriented design to facilitate pedestrian 
path of travel.
b.
Policy C 4.5 Bicycle Improvements. Require new developments to construct or contribute to 
improvements that enhance the cyclist’s experience, including bicycle lanes and bicycle 
parking.
c.
Policy C 6.3 Local Transportation Analysis. Require site-specific transportation impact 
analysis following the City’s adopted Transportation Impact Analysis (TIA) Policy for 
development projects where there may be an adverse condition or effect on the roadway 
system.
The Project will enhance the pedestrian environment by replacing the existing sidewalks with six 
curb cuts/driveways along the site frontage to install new sidewalks with pedestrian-scaled 
lighting, landscape planters with street trees, and new bulb-outs and ADA curb ramps at the 
intersection of San Mateo Drive and State Street and at San Mateo Drive and Villa Terrace. The 
Project will improve the cyclist’s experience by providing 12 short-term and 196 long-term bicycle 
parking spaces and new bike lanes along North San Mateo Drive. 
To demonstrate compliance with Policy C 6.3 and the City’s adopted Transportation Impact 
Analysis (TIA) Policy for development projects, a site-specific transportation impact analysis was 
prepared. The trip generation analysis found that the Project would generate 807 average daily 
trips, with 69 trips (16 inbound and 53 outbound) during the AM peak hour and 69 trips (44 
inbound and 25 outbound) during the PM peak hour. The analysis also concluded that the three 
study intersections would operate at an acceptable Level of Service (LOS) with and without the 
addition of project trips under four scenarios: existing conditions, opening year plus Project, 
cumulative conditions, and cumulative plus the Project. Overall, the LTA found that the Project 
would not result in any significant local traffic or circulation impacts.
3.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of Housing Element 2023-2031.
a.
Policy H 1.5 Encourage Family Housing. Prioritize creation of housing that addresses the 
needs of large families, providing greater housing choice. 
The Project will encourage family housing by expanding housing options in the area for a range of 
household sizes and income levels, such as 1) family housing by providing a range of dwelling sizes

--- page 12 ---
and configurations (including 56 two- and three-bedroom dwellings), and 2) below market and 
market-rate households by providing 19 dwellings reserved for VLI households and 162 for market 
rate households, in a new building supported by residential amenities. 
4.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Community Design and 
Historic Resources Element.
a.
Policy CD 3.2 Replacement Planting. Require appropriate replacement planting or payment 
of an in-lieu fee when protected trees on public or private property are removed.
b.
Policy CD 3.6 New Development Street Trees. Require street tree planting where feasible as 
a condition of all new developments.
c.
Policy CD 4.3 Tribal Consultation. Consult with Native American representatives, including 
through early coordination, to identify locations of importance to Native Americans, including 
archaeological sites, sacred sites, traditional cultural properties, and other types of tribal 
cultural resources. Respect tribal concerns if a tribe has a religious prohibition against 
revealing information about specific practices or locations.
d.
Policy CD 6.8 Public Art. Continue to require public art as part of new development and 
ensure the art is visible and accessible to the public. Support public art as a resource that 
enhances the quality of life for individuals living in, working in, and visiting.
e.
Policy CD 7.3 Multifamily Design. Encourage architectural design of new multifamily 
developments that enhances a neighborhood’s visual and architectural character by providing 
context sensitive building and pedestrian-scale elements, high-quality materials and 
construction, open space, and resident amenities.
f.
Policy CD 7.4 Multifamily Parking. Require new multifamily developments to design and site 
parking to avoid blank, ground-floor walls and to screen views of parking from the street.
g.
Policy CD 7.5 Multifamily Open Space. Require that a portion of required open space for new 
multifamily projects be useable for passive or active recreation.
The Project will plant new street trees along North San Mateo Drive, State Street, and Villa Terrace 
and will be subject to payment of applicable in-lieu fees. Tribal consultation for the Project was 
completed, and the conditions required under AB 130 at the Muwekma Ohlone Tribe’s request 
are included in the Conditions of Approval to avoid significant impacts to tribal cultural resources. 
The Project will support public art to enhance the quality of life for individuals living in, working 
in, and visiting, by paying the in-lieu fees that apply. The Project will enhance the neighborhood’s 
visual and architectural character as demonstrated by compliance with the City’s Objective Design 
Standards.
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR)
1.
The Site Plan and Architectural Review application, per SMMC section 27.08.030(a), may be 
approved, based on the associated Conditions of Approval, and the following findings:
a.
The structures, site plan, and landscaping are in scale and harmonious with the character of 
the neighborhood in that:
i.
The existing development along North San Mateo Drive and within the larger 
neighborhood is primarily low-density, with one to three-story buildings. The 
proposed six-story building that would cover most of the site and contain 181 
dwellings represents a mass and residential density that is much greater than the 
prevailing building form and density in the neighborhood. Nonetheless, the proposed 
building form and residential density reflect the City’s General Plan goals and policies 
to maximize the density and intensity and efficiently use land and infrastructure 
resources (such as Policy LU 1.3).

--- page 13 ---
ii.
The Project proposes a high-quality, contemporary design, incorporating materials 
and details that positively enhance the existing character of the neighborhood and 
surrounding area, as documented by the application of the City’s ODS standards to 
this Project.
b.
The development will not be detrimental to the harmonious and orderly growth of the City in 
that:
i.
In recognition that the existing building form and residential density would not be 
sufficient to meet the City’s Regional Housing Needs Allocation (RHNA), the General 
Plan increased building height and residential density in 10 areas of the City, to 
include this site. The Project supports harmonious and orderly growth in the City by 
proposing a six-story building in compliance with the General Plan’s increased 
building height and residential density. The residential density provided by the Project 
will result in the production of more housing, in particular affordable housing, to help 
meet the City’s current and future needs, as well as help the City make progress 
towards its RHNA obligation. In addition, the building height, mass, and related 
residential density of the Project is consistent with State Density Bonus Law.
ii.
The Project would intensify an underutilized site with a building and uses that fulfill 
the site’s development potential.
iii.
The Project provides higher-density multifamily housing near transit and jobs.
iv.
While the proposed six-story building would be taller and more massive than the 
surrounding development, pursuant to the 2040 General Plan, recent construction in 
the City is transforming low-rise areas with taller, denser development. The increased 
population and street activity that will result from the Project will help improve the 
attractiveness and vitality of the commercial uses in the area and provide housing for 
new residents who wish to live in San Mateo. 
v.
The Project will provide 180 off-street parking spaces, despite being exempted from 
minimum parking standards under State law, to accommodate expected demand for 
residential parking.
vi.
The Project is consistent with the General Plan, Zoning Code, and the City’s Objective 
Design Standards, except where modifications are mandated by State Density Bonus 
Law.
vii.
The Project is in conformance with the Bicycle Master Plan and the Citywide 
Pedestrian Master Plan.
c.
The development will not impair the desirability of investment or occupation in the vicinity, 
and otherwise is in the best interests of the public health, safety, or welfare in that:
i.
The Project represents a significant private investment to produce new housing in an 
area that has not seen significant public or private investment. 
ii.
The Project supports the public health, safety, or welfare of the City by paying 
approximately $5.9 million in development impact fees.
iii.
The Project provides new market-rate and below-market-rate housing to provide new 
users for area businesses, housing for local jobs, and new housing options for the 
community.
iv.
The Project, as conditioned, would not result in any significant impacts to public 
health, safety, or welfare.
v.
The Project provides right-of-way improvements along North San Mateo Drive, State 
Street, and Villa Terrace. 
vi.
The Project will be constructed in compliance with all applicable building and fire 
codes, as well as the City’s building security requirements.

--- page 14 ---
d.
The development meets all applicable standards as adopted by the Planning Commission and 
City Council, conforms with the General Plan, and will correct any violations of the zoning 
ordinance, building code, or other municipal codes that exist on the site, in that:
i.
The Project complies with the applicable General Plan, Zoning Code, and Objective 
Design Standards, and will correct any violations of the Zoning Ordinance or Building 
Code associated with the site by replacing all structures and uses. 
e.
The development will not adversely affect matters regarding police protection, crime 
prevention, and security in that the buildings, paths of travel, and parking facilities will be 
required to conform to the City’s current Security Ordinance through Conditions of Approval, 
in that:
i.
The Project complies with the City’s Security Ordinance by providing a physical 
security plan and a site lighting plan through the Conditions of Approval, which are 
intended to promote crime prevention. 
Site Development Planning Application (SDPA)
1.
The project grading activities are exempt from the requirements for Site Development Planning 
Application per SMMC section 23.40.030(d)(1), as the excavations are within the footprint of the 
building and will only involve building footings and a basement level for parking. Therefore, the 
Site Development Planning Application review is limited to the removal of major vegetation.
2.
All concerns regarding the removal of major vegetation have been addressed, and the Site 
Development Planning Application (SMMC section 23.40.040) and associated Conditions of 
Approval are approved based on the following findings and factors:
a.
Whether the natural landscape and major vegetation is unnecessarily scarred through the 
proposed grading or removal of vegetation;
i.
The Project will not scar a natural landscape, and any major vegetation to be removed 
is only to accommodate the Project.
b.
Review and consideration of the Project is informed by an Arborist Report that was prepared 
in compliance with SMMC Chapters 27.71 and 13.40:
i.
The Project will result in the removal of 19 existing trees, of which four are protected. 
The removal of 17 trees onsite is necessary to facilitate the development of the 
Project. The removal of two trees within the public right-of-way would remove trees 
deemed by the Arborist to be unsuitable in their existing locations.
ii.
All trees will be removed and replaced with appropriate landscaping to both enhance 
the site and create necessary buffers between surrounding properties. 
iii.
All concerns regarding tree removal on the site have been addressed as conditions of 
approval requiring conformance to the City's landscape regulations, through the 
provision of new tree planting as shown on the project plans, and/or through the 
payment of a fee to the City’s tree planting fund.
Vesting Tentative Parcel Map (VTM)
1.
The Project would merge the four parcels into one parcel. Per SMMC section 26.48.060, the 
Planning Commission must deny the Vesting Tentative Parcel Map, if any of the following are true: 
a.
That the proposed map is not consistent with applicable general and specific plans.
b.
That the design or improvement of the proposed subdivision is not consistent with applicable 
general and specific plans.
c.
That the site is not physically suitable for the type of development.
d.
That the site is not physically suitable for the proposed density of development.
e.
That the design of the subdivision or the proposed improvements are likely to cause 
substantial environmental damage or substantially and avoidably injure fish or wildlife or their 
habitat.

--- page 15 ---
f.
That the design of the subdivision or type of improvements is likely to cause serious public 
health problems.
g.
That the design of the subdivision or the type of improvements will conflict with easements, 
acquired by the public at large, for access through or use of, property within the proposed 
subdivision. In this connection, the governing body may approve a map if it finds that 
alternate easements, for access or for use, will be provided, and that these will be 
substantially equivalent to ones previously acquired by the public. This subsection shall apply 
only to easements of record or to easements established by judgment of a court of competent 
jurisdiction and no authority is hereby granted to a legislative body to determine that the 
public at large has acquired easements for access through or use of property within the 
proposed subdivision.
The Planning Commission, based on the findings provided above, finds that the Vesting Tentative 
Parcel Map would facilitate the construction of the building and must be approved because:
i.
The parcel map will facilitate the development of new housing that is consistent with the 
General Plan;
ii.
That the design and improvements associated with the parcel map are consistent with 
applicable general and specific plans;
iii.
The site is suitable for the type (multifamily housing) and density (146.7 dwelling units 
per acre);
iv.
The Project will not result in environmental damage or substantially and avoidably injure 
fish or wildlife or their habitat, because the Project would redevelop a site developed with 
urban uses, that does not provide habitat for fish or wildlife, on a site that is not near a 
body of water or creek, with a new building and use that will be constructed and operated 
in compliance with current standards regarding stormwater, air quality, noise, and 
nighttime lighting;
v.
The design and improvements associated with the parcel map will not cause serious 
public health problems because the Project will be constructed and operated in 
compliance with current standards regarding stormwater, air quality, noise, and 
nighttime lighting; and
vi.
The design and improvements associated with the parcel map will not conflict with any 
easements, as none exist on the subject site, and the City has not identified a need for 
any new easements on or adjacent to the site.
2.
For the reasons stated above, and subject to the associated Conditions of Approval, the Planning 
Commission approves the Vesting Tentative Parcel Map to merge the four parcels into one parcel.

The following conditions of approval apply to the project referenced above. The conditions of approval are 
grouped under specific headings that relate to the timing of required compliance. Additional language within a 
condition may further define the timing of required compliance. Types of Building permits include Demolition, 
Shoring/Excavation, Foundation, and Superstructure.
The following conditions shall be satisfied prior to issuance of a DEMOLITION PERMIT, BUILDING PERMIT FOR 
SHORING OR FOUNDATION, or SITE DEVELOPMENT PERMIT, whichever is issued first, or prior to the deadline 
specified in that condition.
Planning Division (PA)
1.
APPROVED PLANNING APPLICATION CONFORMANCE – All building permit plans, details, and subsequent 
construction shall substantially conform with the approved planning application. This includes but is not 
limited to plans, materials, project description, and other items submitted as part of the approved 
planning application. Any proposed modifications to the approved planning application shall be reviewed 
and approved by the Community Development Director, or their designee, prior to construction of the 
proposed modifications. The Community Development Director, or their designee, shall determine 
whether the proposed modifications substantially conform with the approved planning application, or 
whether a planning application modification is required to be submitted to permit the proposed 
modifications, as required by SMMC section 27.08.080 Modifications. 
2.
BELOW MARKET RATE (BMR) AGREEMENT – In accordance with SMMC section 27.16.050 and 
accompanying BMR Guidelines (Resolution No. 72 – 2025), the applicant shall execute and record a Below 
Market-Rate Housing Agreement. The Agreement shall be consistent with the approved plans. Any 
modifications shall be subject to the approval of the Community Development Director or their designee. 
3.
LIGHTING – The plans submitted for a building permit shall demonstrate that all lighting is energy efficient 
and designed to minimize light pollution and light spillage on adjacent properties, while protecting public 
safety.
4.
PARKING GARAGE – The project plans shall be revised to implement the recommendations provided 
within the Local Traffic Assessment prepared by Hexagon Transportation Consultants, dated March 5, 
2026, to:
(A) Locate the driveway security gate approximately 30 feet from the sidewalk to minimize the effect 
of queueing on the sidewalk and traffic operations on Villa Terrace; and 
(B) Designate all tandem parking spaces for use by the same dwelling.
5.
TENANT RELOCATION ASSISTANCE – Relocation assistance shall be provided to the existing tenant(s) 
occupying each unit to be demolished at the time the subject planning application is filed, consistent with 
SMMC section 27.02.180 as follows:
(A) A list of available comparable housing within San Mateo County;

--- page 18 ---
(B) A relocation allowance in the form of cash or check equal to three times the current monthly 
United States Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) Fair Market Rent for a 
dwelling unit of comparable size and type to the dwelling or room from which the displacement 
occurs; and
(C) A payment not to exceed one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) for actual moving costs and related 
expenses incurred by the tenant household and substantiated by reasonably probative 
documentation.
The Planning Division shall be given notice of the initiation of the tenant relocation process, and shall be 
provided written verification of all compliance with all requirements of this condition subject to the review 
and approval of the Community Development Director, or their designee.
6.
CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL – This complete list of Conditions of Approval shall be reproduced onto the 
second sheet of all building permit plan sets. 
7.

at a minimum, the following components: 
•
Construction timeline (estimated) including major milestones 
•
Construction Phasing Plan
•
Project 24-Hour Liaison and Disturbance Coordinator Name and Contact Information
•
Construction Sign as required in Pre-Construction Meeting Guide
•

Operations (e.g. large concrete pours, crane hoists, etc.)

•
Documentation of Adjacent Street Condition (when applicable) 
•
Traffic Control and Logistic Plan 
•
Road or Sidewalk Closure Plan
•
Construction Hauling Routes 
•
Construction Worker Parking Location and Agreements 
•
Construction Materials and Equipment Staging Plan 
•
Construction Equipment List including compliance with applicable Air Quality and Emission 
Regulations 
•
Erosion and Dust Control Plan 
•
Vibration Monitoring Plan 
•
Construction Noise Mitigation Plan 
•
Vector Control Plan 
A full list of requirements for this document can be found within the construction management plan guide 
available on the City website. Any modification to the approved CMP throughout the construction process 
shall be subject to review and approval by the Community Development Director or their designee 
8.
EXCAVATED SOILS – The applicant shall submit a compliance letter from San Mateo County Environmental 
Health Services to the Planning Division subject to the satisfaction of the Community Development 
Director, or their designee. The compliance letter shall indicate that site soils have been tested prior to 
disposal to confirm that the concentration of constituents present in site soils do not exceed hazardous 
waste criteria of local, state and federal regulations. If the concentration of constituents in the project site 
soils exceed hazardous waste criteria, the letter shall also confirm that the soils will be disposed of in 
accordance with local, state, and federal regulations.

planning application fees.

applicant.  
11.
TRIBAL CULTURAL RECORDS SEARCH – Prior to issuance of any permit associated with implementation of

Building Division (PA)
12.
ADDRESS ASSIGNMENT – The applicant shall submit an address assignment application for the proposed

APPLICABLE BUILDING STANDARDS AND LOCAL CODES – All building permit plans shall demonstrate

the Building Division at the time of filing the building permit application.

job number (J#) from Bay Area Air Quality Management District (BAAQMD).

DEMOLITION – A building permit for demolition shall be issued in accordance with SMMC section 
23.06.100, to the satisfaction of the Building Official or his/her designee. 
16.
PRE-CONSTRUCTION CONFERENCE FOR LARGE PROJECTS – A pre-construction conference shall be held at 
a time and location agreed upon by the City and applicant for the purpose of reviewing Conditions of 
Approval and construction-site procedures. The applicant shall be represented by his design and 
construction staff, which include any sub-contractors. Departments having conditions of approval for the 
project will represent the City. This meeting shall be held prior to issuance of the Demolition Permit, 
Building Permit or Site Development Permit, and shall be satisfied prior to issuance of whichever permit 
is issued first.

SITE SURVEY – The applicant shall provide a full site survey stamped and signed by a Land Surveyor 
licensed by the State of California. The survey shall include, but not be limited to: location and dimensions 
of property lines, location of streets and easements, existing buildings, topographic contour lines, 
trees/landscape, and other structures.

Fire Department (PA)

Public Works Department (PA)

ENCROACHMENT PERMITS, BONDS, AND INSURANCE – For any work within the Public Right of Way or

21.
TRAFFIC CONTROL & SITE LOGISTICS PLANS – The applicant shall submit traffic control plans for any impact

Requirements.

contour elevations, drainage patterns, flow lines, slopes, and all other property encumbrances. 
 
23.
GRADING DEPOSITS – Prior to permit issuance, the Applicant shall provide refundable grading security 
deposit funds or bond to the City based upon the Comprehensive Fee Schedule in effect at the time of 
building permit submittal. The Applicant shall be required to increase the deposit if revisions to the 
approved plans increase the proposed earthwork activities. After substantial completion and stabilization 
of the site, to the satisfaction of the Director of Public Works or designee, the City will refund any portion 
of the deposit not utilized by the City or release the bond. 
24.
STORMWATER POLLUTION PREVENTION PERMIT – In accordance with SMMC section 7.39.170, the 
applicant shall obtain a Stormwater Pollution Prevention (STOPPP) Construction permit for all work 
associated with stormwater pollution prevention, pay the required fees and post the required cash 
deposit. The fee amount will be based upon the Comprehensive Fee Schedule in effect at the time the 
building permit application is submitted. The Applicant shall be required to increase the deposit, at the 
discretion of the City, for any associated costs in excess of the deposit. Prior to final occupancy, the bill 
shall be paid in full. The City will refund any portion of the deposit not utilized. 
25.
CONSTRUCTION GENERAL PERMIT – For construction activities that will disturb one (1) acre or more, the

Permit and a Storm Water Pollution Prevention Plan (SWPPP) prepared by a qualified SWPPP designer to 
Public Works.

27.
SEWER ANALYSIS AND IMPROVEMENT – Prior to building permit issuance, the Applicant shall perform a 
flow monitoring study to assess the actual existing flows along the 8 inch sewer main in San Mateo Drive 
from Villa Terrace to Williams Place. The study will monitor three sewer manholes: MH 179-46X at the 
intersection of San Mateo Drive & Bellevue Ave, and two manholes at the San Mateo Drive & Williams 
Place intersection, MH 179-02X & MH 179-41X. The developer shall provide that study to the City for the 
City to complete a supplementary sewer analysis on the project’s impact on the sewer main. If the 
project's proposed peak flow will cause the sewer main to exceed the City’s threshold of 3 feet of 
freeboard at any structure in San Mateo Drive, between Villa Terrace and Williams Place, per the Sewer

--- page 21 ---
System Master Plan Element 5, then the Applicant shall construct sewer improvements through open-
trench method for upsizing main line to mitigate the impact. The scope for any public sewer 
improvements shall be permitted with or prior to the building permit issuance.

Recorder’s Office prior to the issuance of any City permits. 
Prior to the City’s release of the parcel map to the title company, the applicant may, at the discretion of 
the Director of Public Works or designee, be required to submit to the City an electronic copy of the map 
in PDF and AutoCAD.

provide security for the remaining public improvements to be completed. The agreement will be 
forwarded to the City Council for approval per SMMC Chapter 3.60.

Police Department (PA)
49.
PUBLIC SAFETY COMMUNICATIONS FOR TALL BUILDINGS – The building permit plans for the 
superstructure shall show compliance with Security Code SMMC “23.54.020 CITY COMMUNICATION 
SYSTEMS – HIGH RISE BUILDINGS”, by providing for the following allowances for the placement of 
emergency communications equipment on the building permit plans:
(A) Enough enclosed space for the equivalent of one dedicated server rack in a locked server room 
that is clean, dry, and well-ventilated (this does not need to be a fire control room); 
(B) One four-inch conduit from the designated server rack through the roof. The conduit shall be 
provided with wide radius bends, a weatherhead on the roof, and a pull string and ring; 
(C) Authorization to mount antennas on the roof. The maximum allowable distance from the 
designated server rack to the antenna mounting location shall be 100 feet; 
(D) One 20-amp, 120 VAC dedicated electrical circuit on the building’s emergency generator. An 
uninterruptable power supply (UPS) may be installed by the City if the building is not provided 
with an emergency generator; 
(E) 12 copper cable pairs to the building’s main telephone terminal; and, 
(F) Ground buss bar bonded to the building grounding system. 
This requirement is in addition to the requirement of the California Fire Code to supply a functional 
emergency responder radio coverage system. 
50.
RESIDENTIAL PARKING GARAGE SECURITY – The building permit plans for the superstructure shall show: 
(A) Restricted access to the parking garage with electrically operated closures to allow passage of 
motor vehicles at all times. Required visitor parking shall have unrestricted access. The closures,

--- page 24 ---
whether overhead, sliding or swinging, shall be provided with reopening devices which will function to 
stop and reopen the closure in case the closure is obstructed when closing. Openings into the garage 
which are not for vehicular or human passage shall be provided with security grilles or screens. 
(B) Digital keypads shall be provided to allow for entry by services and emergency services vehicles 
into the garages at all times. Exterior doors or gates providing access into the secure areas of the 
parking garage shall remain locked at all times, and shall only be accessible through the use of 
keys, key fob or remote keyless entry system devices furnished to the building residents. 
Pedestrian access points exiting out of garage shall also be accessible through the use of keys 
furnished to the building residents and shall be equipped with self-closing devices. All storage, 
maintenance, and trash rooms within parking garages shall have doors which cannot be locked 
from the inside, and that close and lock quickly and automatically upon exit. 
(C) Parking spaces shall not be numbered to coincide with interior unit numbers. 
(D) Lighting in the parking garage shall be in conformance with the Security Ordinance as it applies to 
SITE LIGHTING. No dark areas shall exist inside the parking garage 
51.
SECURED BUILDING ACCESS BY EMERGENCY PERSONNEL – The building permit plans for the 
superstructure shall show the detailed specifications for and the installation of telephone entry pads 
(TEPs) and/or wireless “click to enter” systems at the main exterior building entrance(s) and parking 
garage entrance(s) for secured buildings. These access systems must allow emergency personnel to access 
all levels of the interior of the building. The access systems must also be installed at exterior gate locations 
that lead to secured areas of the site, such as interior courtyards. Access system placement location is 
subject to the review and approval of the Chief of Police or their designee, prior to the approval of the 
first building permit for the project. Police access codes shall be as provided by the Chief of Police or their 
designee at the time of installation.

Public Works Department (PA)
53.
C3 COMPLIANCE – The project shall provide stormwater controls and treatment measures in compliance 
with the requirements of the Municipal Regional Permit NPDES Permit # CAS612008 and the San Mateo 
County C.3 Stormwater Technical Guidance. The project’s grading, drainage, and treatment designs shall 
be in substantial conformance with the approved plans and subject to the final approval of the Director 
of Public Works or designee.
The project plans shall include a Stormwater Management Plan that identifies the project site area, new 
and/or replaced pervious and impervious areas, drainage management areas, treatment measures, sizing 
calculations, source controls and site design measures implemented, saturated hydraulic conductivity 
rates at relevant locations or hydrologic soil type (A, B, C, or D) and information sources, elevations of 
seasonal high groundwater table, and a summary of how the project complies with C.3 requirements.
Treatment measures shall be sized to accommodate runoff their full tributary drainage area or provide a 
separate bypass system such that the treatment measure is not surcharged and act as a bypass.  
54.
DRAINAGE – The project shall be designed to maintain or reduce the stormwater runoff peak flow at each 
of the project’s discharge point(s) to the public storm drain system. The project shall direct all runoff

--- page 25 ---
directly to the City’s storm drain system without passing through adjacent properties not part of this 
project. Applicant shall submit plans, drawings, and storm calculations to demonstrate the design 
complies with these requirements. 
55.
GARBAGE/RECYCLE/COMPOSTING STORAGE AND SERVICE – The applicant shall provide an adequate area 
for the purposes of storing garbage, recycling, composting collection containers for scheduled servicing 
by the franchise solid waste collection service. The containers shall be placed at the service location 
allowing enough room for the truck to safely approach the containers. The collection containers shall be 
brought to the service area and returned to the storage enclosure by the property owner. The containers 
are not to be in public view or in the public right-of-way prior to, or beyond the scheduled service times. 
An approved letter from the City’s franchise solid waste collection service provider stating that service is 
available to the project as designed has been received. Any revisions made to the approved letter shall be 
reflected in the building permit plans. The building permit plans for the superstructure shall show garbage 
and recycling areas. 
56.
INITIAL STORM AND SANITARY SEWER ASSESSMENT – The applicant shall perform an initial inspection (via 
remote TV camera) of the mainline storm and sanitary sewer from the nearest upstream structure to the 
nearest downstream structure of the project’s point of connections. During the initial inspection, any 
damage must be reported to the Department of Public Works. The applicant shall perform the same 
inspection once construction is completed. Damage in result of this project’s construction shall be 
repaired by the applicant at their expense.

possible.

59.
STREETLIGHTS PHOTOMETRICS – The applicant shall provide a lighting “photometrics” plan for streetlights 
in the public right-of-way with the civil plans. The lighting plan shall comply with the following: 
(A) Be based on photometric analysis consistent with the Illuminating Engineering Society’s (IES) 
Recommended Practice For Design And Maintenance Of Roadway And Parking Facility Lighting 
(ANSI/IES RP-8-18) and achieve the required lighting levels using the least number of luminaires 
possible, using a consistent pattern of luminaire placement, and shall include luminaires on both 
sides of the street if such a pattern reduces the number of luminaires required, unless otherwise 
approved by the City. Utilize the City’s list of standard luminaires at the time of design for selection 
of any new or replacement luminaires proposed by the project. 
(B) Include a design for lighting all public streets, intersections, sidewalks, pedestrian paths, and 
bicycle facilities located in the public roadway right-of-way adjacent to the project site to meet 
the lighting levels per the photometric analysis. 
(C) Include only City owned streetlights within the public right-of-way, or located in an easement on 
private property, unless otherwise approved by the City. 
(D) Include pedestrian scale lighting if pedestrian scale lighting is already in use on the block of the 
project frontage, or if the City’s Pedestrian Master Plan recommends pedestrian scale lighting on 
the project frontage.

--- page 26 ---
(E) Include separate analysis zones for each street, each sidewalk by frontage, and each intersection, 
configured according to the City’s standard practice in use at the time the analysis is begun. Show 
each photometric analysis zone with point illuminance values.
(F) Include the following information about each luminaire included in the analysis:
1)
Location
2)
Type (Indicated by the City’s specification name)
3)
Mounting height
4)
Arm length
5)
Total luminaire Light Loss Factor (LLF) 
(G) Include a table displaying the following values for the analysis zones:
1)
Average Maintained Illuminance (fc)
2)
Average Uniformity Ratio
3)
Maximum Uniformity Ratio
4)
Maximum Point Illuminance Value (fc)
5)
Minimum Point Illuminance Value (fc)
(H) Maintain the following minimum spacing between luminaires:
1)
50 feet between pedestrian scale luminaires on the same side of the street.
2)
100 feet between all other types of luminaires on the same side of the street.
3)
50 feet between luminaires of mixed types.
4)
Reduced spacing may be approved by the City if the photometric analysis indicates it is 
necessary to meet the required lighting levels.
(I) Lighting Level Requirements (Illuminance Method)
-
N San Mateo Dr – Road: 1.3 fc Average, 3.0 Average Uniformity Ratio, 5.0 Max Uniformity 
Ratio
-
N San Mateo Dr – Sidewalk: 0.5 fc Average, 4.0 Average Uniformity Ratio
-
State St – Road: 0.7 fc Average, 6.0 Average Uniformity Ratio, 10.0 Max Uniformity Ratio
-
State St – Sidewalk: 0.5 fc Average, 4.0 Average Uniformity Ratio
-

-

-

PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS – The applicant shall have improvement plans prepared for all work in the public 
right-of-way or easements by a licensed civil engineer. The improvement plans shall substantially conform 
to the approved planning application and shall be approved by the Director of Public Works or designee. 
All work within the City’s right of way shall be designed and constructed to the City Standards and 
Specifications unless otherwise noted. All public improvements shall be completed prior to the issuance 
of the final Certificate of Occupancy.
An Encroachment Permit shall be required for all public improvements in the public right-of-way or 
easements. All work shown on the improvement plans shall be inspected and approved by Public Works. 
The developer shall repair or replace all existing or new improvements that were damaged or removed 
because of developer’s operations.
The public improvement plans shall show the following public improvements in the public right of way: 
(A) SIGNAGE AND STRIPING – The applicant shall install traffic signage and striping of a material and 
design approved by the Director of Public Works or designee and replace any that are damaged 
during construction. These include but are not limited to all pavement markings, painted curbs 
and handicap markings. All permanent pavement markings shall be thermoplastic. Color and

--- page 27 ---
location of painted curbs shall be shown on the plans and subject to approval by the Director of 
Public Works or designee. Any existing painted curb or pavement markings no longer required 
shall be removed by grinding if thermoplastic, sand blasting if in paint. Once installed, the 
applicant shall coordinate with City crews to mark any red curb within the proposed City right-of-
way with a City seal. The Solid Waste Collection staging area utilizes the loading zone located in 
the City right-of-way and the applicant shall install yellow curb and appropriate signage to 
facilitate service times.
(B) LOADING ZONE IN THE PUBLIC ROW – The applicant shall install a loading zone as shown on the 
approved plans along State St. 
(C) SIDEWALK – The applicant shall replace all sidewalk fronting the project site with A.5. Sidewalk 
Standards – Residential Type C New Development from the City’s Pedestrian Master Plan. 
Sidewalk replacement shall be constructed per current City Standard. Sidewalks fronting the 
project property must comply to Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA) standards. 
(D) CURB RAMPS – The applicant shall construct curb ramp(s) in accordance with Caltrans Standard 
Plan A88A at N San Mateo Dr & State St and N San Mateo Dr & Villa Terrace. The actual ramp 
“Case” shall be identified on the plans and shall be approved by the Director of Public Works or 
designee or designee. 
(E) CURB AND GUTTER – The applicant shall replace to existing City standards all curb and gutter 
fronting the project site and as required for restoration purposes. New curb and gutter shall be 
constructed per current City Standard, or as otherwise shown on the approved plan set. 
(F) DRIVEWAY APPROACH – The applicant shall install City Standard Commercial driveway approach 
on Villa Terrace as shown on the approved plans. The applicant shall install a short apron along 
State St to facilitate the Solid Waste Staging Area as shown on the approved plans. The applicant 
shall install pedestrian warning system at project driveway.
(G) SEWER LATERAL – The applicant shall install two 6 inch minimum City Standard sewer lateral 
connections from the property line to the sewer main located on N San Mateo Dr. The installation 
shall be done in accordance with City Standard Drawings. 
(H) SANITARY SEWER MANHOLES – The applicant shall install two standard sanitary sewer manholes 
on N San Mateo Dr, per approved plans and in accordance with City Standard Drawings.
(I) STORM WATER CONNECTION – The applicant shall connect to the City storm main along State St 
at two points using wye connections, in accordance with City Standard Drawings, as shown on the 
approved plans.
(J) STORM WATER CATCH BASIN – The applicant shall replace existing catch basin at the proposed 
bioretention along Villa Terrace to include overflow drain inlet per approved plans and in 
accordance with City Standard Details.
(K) STREETLIGHTING IMPROVEMENTS – The applicant shall provide streetlight improvement plans 
with the civil plans a The Streetlight Improvement Plan shall: 
1)
Implement the project’s Lighting Plan from their project frontage to the roadway 
centerline.
2)
Implement improvements beyond the project frontage or the roadway centerline if such 
improvements are necessary to provide a functioning lighting system.
3)
Show all work necessary to construct the streetlight improvements for which the project 
is responsible to implement.
4)
Include all electrical calculations (i.e. voltage drop) required for design of a functional 
streetlight system that complies with all applicable codes and standards.
5)
Shows location of connection to existing streetlight circuit(s).
6)
Shows location of proposed new electrical service connections.
7)
Include a map showing the full extent of all streetlight circuits that will include project 
lighting improvements. This map shall include information necessary for verifying voltage

--- page 28 ---
drop calculations and may also be used for submittal to the serving utility as part of an 
electrical service modification application. At a minimum the map shall include:
a.
Location and wattage of all streetlight luminaires on the circuit.
b.
Streetlight pole numbers.
c.
Length of conduit runs used for voltage drop calculations. Lengths may be labeled 
directly on the plan view or presented in a conduit run schedule.
It shall be the applicant’s responsibility to verify the location of all existing streetlight equipment 
and infrastructure, including, but not limited to, underground conduits, pull boxes, poles, and 
electrical service connections, as needed for the preparation of the Lighting Plan and the 
Streetlight Improvement Plan. The applicant shall be responsible for coordinating all lighting 
improvements with the serving utility, including preparing all required documents and 
attachments, attending all field meetings requested by the serving utility, submitting applications 
for new or modified electrical service.
The applicant shall be responsible for all costs charged by the serving utility associated with the 
project’s streetlight improvements, including but not limited to application fees, permit fees, 
engineering charges, and construction charges.

TRIANGULAR AREA OF VISIBILITY – Per the approved plan set and Local Transportation Analysis

corner meets the requirements of a minimum vertical clearance of 7 feet, and/or are less than 3 feet in

UNDERGROUND (OR COVERED) PARKING GARAGE DRAINAGE – The building permit plans for the

the project shall not discharge to these garage drains. The design shall be done by a licensed Civil Engineer

who shall provide hydraulic calculations and drawings subject to the approval of the Director of Public

UNDERGROUND UTILITY SERVICES – The building permit plans for the superstructure shall show the
