67.
UTILITIES – Utility plans shall be submitted as part of the building permit plans for the superstructure and 
shall show appropriate line types and labels to identify different type of utilities and pipe sizes. Clearly 
identify both existing and proposed public and private utilities.
The Developer shall provide joint trench composite plans for the underground electrical, gas, telephone, 
cable television, and communication conduits and cables including the size, location and details of all 
trenches, locations of building utility service stubs and meters and placements or arrangements of 
junction structures.
Sanitary sewer laterals and/or water meters located in driveways shall have traffic rated boxes and lids.
Developer is required to confirm the location of existing utility lines along the project frontage by 
potholing. Prior to any potholing, developer shall obtain an encroachment permit and submit a pothole 
plan for City review and approval. Developer shall provide the pothole results to the Director of Public 
Works or designee or designee prior to final design. Any utility conflicts shall be the responsibility of the 
developer to rectify. 
68.
WASTEWATER CAPACITY CHARGE – A wastewater capacity charge, as established by SMMC section 
7.38.065, is imposed on all new development to recover a proportionate share of costs for existing and 
future wastewater system facilities and assets from new or expanded connections to City wastewater 
systems. The applicable wastewater capacity charge is determined by use, wastewater flow, and 
wastewater strength loadings and the amount shall be established by City Council resolution. The fee shall 
be collected by the Public Works Department and paid prior to issuance of the first superstructure building 
permit. The fee shall be based on the City’s adopted Comprehensive Fee Schedule. 
69.
WILL SERVE LETTER FOR WATER – A Will Serve Letter from the water company shall be supplied to the 
Director of Public Works or designee.  
70.
ENCROACHMENT AND MAINTENANCE AGREEMENT – Applicant shall enter into a City-approved 
Encroachment and Maintenance agreement for the improvements encroaching into a Public Utility 
Easement or public right of way prior to the issuance of the building permit. The applicant shall have the 
agreement recorded against the owner’s property that indemnifies and holds harmless the City, its elected 
and appointed officials, employees and agents. The agreement shall include language in which the 
applicant agrees to allow access to any utility company wishing to have access to the public right-of-way 
for existing or new utility installation. The agreement shall also include language that requires the removal 
of the improvements, at the owner’s expense, should the City desire to use the right-of-way for street, 
sidewalk or other purposes identified by the Director of Public Works or designee. The agreement shall 
be approved as to form by the City Attorney’s Office and shall be recorded against the owner’s property 
prior to the issuance of any City encroachment permit.

The following conditions shall be complied with AT ALL TIMES DURING THE CONSTRUCTION PHASE OF THE 
PROJECT.
Planning Division (PA)
71.
CONSTRUCTION MANAGEMENT PLAN COMPLIANCE – The applicant shall implement and remain in full 
compliance with the approved Construction Management Plan throughout all phases of construction. All 
construction activities shall be conducted in a manner consistent with the approved plan. Any deviation 
from, or modification to the approved Construction Management Plan shall require prior review and 
approval by the Community Development Director or their designee. Consistent with the requirements of 
the CMP, construction disturbances reports shall be submitted monthly to provide timely updates on 
project impacts. 
Violations of any portion of the approved Construction Management Plan or other applicable construction 
management requirement may result in the issuance of a “Stop Work Order”. 
72.
FRAME/PLANNING ROUGH INSPECTION – Upon completion of all framing and prior to the installation of 
exterior sheathing and windows, the applicant shall request the Project Planner conduct a Rough Frame 
inspection to verify items including, but not limited to, window locations, window sizes, and massing. The 
applicant shall contact the Project Planner to schedule each inspection a minimum of 72 hours in advance 
of the requested inspection. 
73.
PALEONTOLOGICAL RESOURCES – In the event of the discovery of paleontological resources (fossils) 
whether on-site or in the public right-of-way, the applicant shall halt all construction activities within 50 
feet of the discovery, notify the Planning Manager and/or Project Planner, and retain a qualified 
paleontologist to determine the significance of the discovery. The paleontologist shall evaluate the 
uniqueness of the find, prepare a written report documenting the find and recommending further courses 
of action, and submit a summary of findings to the Project Planner. The applicant shall incorporate the 
recommendations of the paleontologist when continuing construction. 
Building Division (PA)
74.
CONSTRUCTION WORK HOURS – Construction shall occur only between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 7:00 
p.m. on Monday through Friday, between 9:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m. on Saturday, and between 12:00 noon 
and 4:00 p.m. on Sundays and holidays. These hours do not apply to construction that takes place inside 
a completely enclosed building and does not exceed the exterior ambient noise level as measured 10 feet 
from the exterior property lines. The applicant shall conform to the construction work hours to control 
traffic congestion, noise, and dust unless an exemption is granted in accordance with SMMC section 
23.06.061. 
Fire Department (PA)
75.
ADDRESS NUMBERS – The applicant shall post temporary address numbers on each building at the project 
site that must be easily visible from the street or fire access road. 
76.
DEMOLITION – The applicant shall comply with the California Fire Code Chapter 33 during all phases of 
construction of the project.  
77.
EGRESS – The applicant shall maintain required egress for all adjacent buildings/properties.  
78.
STANDPIPES – For projects that require standpipes by California Fire Code section 905.3.1, the applicant 
shall provide not less than one standpipe for use during construction or demolition.

Best Management Practices.

Planning Division (PA)

APPROVED PLANNING APPLICATION CONFORMANCE AT ALL TIMES – All physical improvements, uses, and 
operational requirements authorized by the approved planning application shall, at all times that the use 
permitted by this planning application occupies the premises, substantially conform with the approved 
planning application. This includes but is not limited to plans, materials, project description, and other

submitted to permit the proposed modifications, as required by SMMC section 27.08.080. 
95.
COMPLIANCE WITH REGULATIONS FOR DISCOVERY OF HUMAN REMAINS – The project shall comply with 
Health and Safety Code section 7050.5 and Public Resources Code section 5097.98, including immediate 
work stoppage upon discovery of human remains or burial grounds, and treatment in accordance 
with applicable law and in consultation with the affected California Native American tribe.  
96.
DOCUMENTATION OF TRIBAL CULTURAL RESOURCES – All treatment and documentation of tribal cultural 
resources shall be conducted in a culturally appropriate manner, as required by Public Resources Code 
section 21080.66. (AB130).

GENERAL PLAN COMPLIANCE – Unless otherwise approved through the entitlement process, the project 
shall be designed, constructed, and operated in a manner that is consistent with all applicable goals, 
policies, land use designations, and development standards of the City’s adopted General Plan 2040. 
98.
LABOR CODE – The provisions of Labor Code section 218.8 shall extend to the development proponent in 
addition to the direct contractor or subcontractor. The development proponent for this project 
is Prometheus Real Estate Group, Inc.   
99.
TRIBAL CULTURAL RESOURCES – Tribal cultural resources shall be avoided where feasible, in accordance 
with Public Resources Code section 21084.3(a). In furtherance of this requirement, where feasible, the 
project applicant shall provide deference to tribal preferences regarding access to spiritual, ceremonial, 
and burial sites, and incorporate tribal traditional knowledge in the protection and sustainable use of 
tribal cultural resources and landscapes.  
100.
TRIBAL ECOLOGICAL KNOWLEDGE – An application of tribal ecological knowledge into any habitat 
restoration efforts shall be undertaken by the project proponent as applicable to the specific 
environmental context and conditions of the project.  
101.
TRIBAL MONITOR – The project shall include tribal monitoring during all ground-disturbing activities, as 
follows:  
(A) One monitor as designated by the Muwekma Oholone Tribe shall be present during all ground-
disturbing activities and for all mechanical ground-disturbing/subsurface excavations that have 
the potential to affect native soils that could potentially contain Tribal cultural deposits within the 
entire construction project area, including off-site related improvements.  
(B) The tribal monitor shall comply with applicant’s site access and workplace safety requirements.

--- page 34 ---
(C) The applicant shall compensate the tribal monitor at a rate provided in Muwekma rate sheet, 
determined in good faith, that aligns with customary compensation for cultural resource 
monitoring, taking into account factors such as the scope and duration of the project, as well as 
the tribal monitor’s actual time spent on the project site during ground-disturbing activities.  
City Attorney (PA)

INDEMNIFICATION – The applicant shall defend, indemnify, and hold harmless the City of San Mateo, its

attorney fees that might result from third party challenge. If applicant is required to defend the City, the 
City shall retain the right to select the counsel who shall defend the City.

forth in SMMC Chapter 1.04-General Penalty, as well as any other available legal remedies. 
Police Department (PA)

BUILDING SECURITY CODE COMPLIANCE – The building permit plans shall comply with the City’s Building 
Security Code (SMMC Chapter 23.54).  
105.
PUBLIC SAFETY COMMUNICATIONS FOR TALL BUILDINGS, ACCESS AND SECURITY – The applicant shall 
allow 24-hour, 7 day per week access to the dedicated public safety communications radio server rack 
and antenna(s) for maintenance purposes at all times that the use permitted by this planning application 
occupies the premises. If the City installs radio equipment, the applicant shall take reasonable measures 
to secure and safeguard City equipment from theft or vandalism. 
106.
SITE LIGHTING STANDARDS – Exterior security lighting in compliance with the Building Security Code 
“Exterior Security Lighting” (SMMC section 23.54.060) shall be provided and maintained at all times that 
the use permitted by this planning application occupies the premises. Site lighting shall comply with the 
requirement of an average illuminance of 1 foot-candle, a minimum illuminance of 0.3 foot-candle, and a 
uniformity ratio not to exceed 4:1 average to minimum. Light sources shall be capable of producing a 
“bright white” light with a color temperature between 3000K and 4000K and a color rendering index (CRI) 
of at least 65 unless otherwise approved. This lighting standard is applicable to all parking lots, driveways, 
circulation areas, aisles, passageways, recesses, and grounds contiguous to all buildings. The lighting 
system shall be so designed as to limit light spill beyond property lines and to shield the light source from 
view from off site. 
107.
VIDEO SURVEILLANCE STANDARDS – The applicant shall install and operate for the life of the project a 
video surveillance system subject to the following requirements: 
(A) The information shall be maintained and retrievable for a minimum of 30 days. The captured video 
material shall be accessible to investigating police personnel through some form of facility 
management during regular business hours. The applicant shall provide proof of registration of 
the video surveillance camera system with the City through the City’s Neighborhood Eyes Security 
Team web form (https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/forms.aspx?FID=134). 
(B) Cameras shall be placed and maintained to view common areas of the property accessible to the 
public such as lobbies, parking lots, parking garages and entrances and exits to all parking garages, 
gates dividing different uses inside mixed-use parking garages, driveways, circulation areas, aisles, 
passageways, recesses, and grounds contiguous to all buildings. This condition is not intended to 
require Applicant to install pole mount cameras on the property, cameras to view these areas 
may be installed on the building facing out.

--- page 35 ---
(C) The cameras in this system shall be megapixel or better CCTV cameras that shall be capable of 
operating in all lighting conditions anticipated at project completion. Cameras viewing locations 
intended to allow routine vehicle passage onto the sites and/or garages shall additionally be 
capable of capturing the front and rear of all entering and exiting vehicles that use the sites and/or 
garages, and be of sufficient quality to identify the make and model of vehicles accessing the site, 
clearly read both front and rear license plates of vehicles, and clearly depict faces of occupants 
through the front windshield. 
108.
PHOTOMETRIC PLAN SUBMITTAL REQUIREMENT – The building permit plans for the superstructure shall 
include a photometric plan showing the installation of lighting fixtures and lighting levels to be reviewed 
and approved by the Chief of Police or their designee. The photometric plan shall include point-by-point 
lighting levels in foot-candles for the entire plot and ten feet beyond the project property lines. The point-
by-point photometric plan shall provide lighting levels on a grid not to exceed five feet by five feet across 
the entire site. Each point shall report the illuminance to the nearest 0.1 foot-candles. Photometric 
calculations including maximum foot-candles, average foot-candles, minimum foot-candles, average to 
minimum uniformity, and maximum to minimum uniformity shall be included on the plan submitted. 
Select specifications for fixtures selected shall be provided on the photometric plan sufficient to ensure 
compliance with the SITE LIGHTING STANDARDS. 
Public Works Department (PA)
109.
POST CONSTRUCTION BEST MANAGEMENT PRACTICES (BMP) – In accordance with the City’s Storm Water 
Management and Discharge Control Rules and Regulations, SMMC Chapter 7.39, and the San Mateo 
Countywide Stormwater Management Plan (SWMP) by reference, the applicant shall:
(A) Owner/occupant shall inspect private stormwater treatment devices and GI features in the public 
right-of-way at least two (2) times per year and sweep parking lots immediately prior to and once 
during the storm season.
(B) The applicant shall pay a fee on a yearly basis for cost associated with, but not limited to, City 
inspection of the private stormwater treatment facilities, emergency maintenance needed to 
protect public health or watercourses, and facility replacement or repair in the event that the 
treatment facility is no longer able to meet performance standards or has deteriorated. The fee 
shall be based upon the City’s adopted Comprehensive Fee Schedule.
(C) Label new and redeveloped storm drain inlets with the phrase “No Dumping – Drains to Bay” 
plaques to alert the public to the destination of storm water and to prevent direct discharge of 
pollutants into the storm drain. Template ordering information is available from the Department 
of Public Works.
(D) All process equipment, oils fuels, solvents, coolants, fertilizers, pesticides, and similar chemical 
products, as well as petroleum based wastes, tallow, and grease planned for storage outdoors 
shall be stored in covered containers at all times. 
110.
TRANSPORTATION DEMAND MANAGEMENT (TDM) Checklist – Once implemented, the Transportation 
Demand Management Checklist shall be monitored and assessed annually for the occupied life of the 
development. The checklist shall be recorded with the County. The assessment of compliance with the 
Transportation Demand Management Checklist shall be submitted to Public Works by the end of every 
calendar year (December 31st).

EXHIBIT B
SUMMARY OF PROJECT WAIVERS
The waivers to the following standards have been identified, to be applied pursuant to State Density Bonus Law:
1)
Floor Area and a Floor Area Ratio – For the E2-1.5 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.48.060(c), 
the FAR limit is 1.5. The Project would result in an FAR of 3.9. 
2)
Floor Area and a Floor Area Ratio – For the C3-2 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.34.050(b), the 
FAR limit is 2.0. The Project would result in an FAR of 3.9.
3)
Residential Density – The San Mateo General Plan 2040 Land Use Designation for this site is Residential 
Medium II, and the maximum base density is 99 dwellings per acre. For this 1.22-acre site, the maximum 
density is 120.7 dwellings. The proposed Project would include 181 dwelling units, exceeding the 
maximum density. However, the Project would reserve 15% of the base density (19 dwellings, or 15.7% 
of the General Plan maximum) for Very-Low Income (VLI) households. Per Government Code section 
65915(f)(2), a project with at least 15% of the dwellings reserved for VLI households is eligible for a density 
bonus of 50% of the base density. The 50% bonus applied to this site would increase the maximum 
allowable density to 182 dwellings (the General Plan density for this site is 120.7dwellings, and per 
Government Code section 65915(q), the density is rounded up to 121 dwellings. The 50% bonus, when 
applied to this density, would allow 181.5 dwellings, and per Government Code section 65915(q), the total 
number of dwellings allowed for this site is rounded up to 182 dwellings). While this Project would be 
eligible for a density increase to accommodate up to 182 dwellings, it proposes only 181.
4)
Yards – For the E2-1.5 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.48.090, the yard along each street frontage 
must be at least 7.5 feet. The Project would not provide a yard along North San Mateo Drive or Villa 
Terrace.
5)
Buffers-Rear yard – For the C3-2 portion of the site, per SMMC sections 27.34.060, 27.30.060(a) & 
27.22.080(c), the minimum yard is 25 feet along the portion of the site that abuts the R-zoned property. 
The Project would provide a 2-foot yard abutting the R-zoned property.
6)
Buffer-Landscape – For the E2-1.5 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.48.100, a landscape buffer of 
at least one-half the height of the proposed building (or approx. 38 feet) must be provided along Villa 
Terrace and for the portion of the site that abuts the R-zoned property. The Project would not provide a 
landscape buffer along Villa Terrace and would provide a 2-foot buffer, with landscaping to be provided 
via hanging vines, abutting the adjacent R-zoned property. 
7)
Parcel Coverage-Open Space – For the E2-1.5 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.48.065, at-grade 
open space must be at least 20% of the parcel area. The Project would not provide at-grade open space.
8)
Blank Walls – Per ODS section 4.1.1, “Blank walls shall be limited to a maximum of twenty (20) feet in 
length on all stories”. The ground-floor wall facing the residential district to the southwest would be over 
10 feet in height (13 feet to 21 feet is proposed), the horizontal length would be greater than 20 feet (326 
linear feet is proposed), and the ground-floor wall would not include a transparent window or door.

3 TABLES
187
TOTAL
9789
*MAXIMUM AREAS BASED ON 181 UNITS
MINIMUM PARK SPACE NEEDED: 8,233 sf
PARK SPACE PROVIDED:  9,789 sf
SWIMMING POOL AREA
1.
POOL IS TOTALLY FENCED.
2.
POOL DECK IS INCLUDED AT NO MORE THAN  2 X THE WATER
SURFACE AREA.
3.
ACTUAL POOL WATER DIMENSION IS NOT LESS THAN 15’ IN
SMALLEST HORIZONTAL DIMENSION. POOL DECK INCLUDES THE
SPA AREA.
RECREATION BUILDING
1.
SIZE INCLUDES HALLWAY, STORAGE, LOCKER AND RESTROOM
FACILITIES THAT SERVE NO OTHER USE THAN RECREATION
PURPOSES THAT TAKE PLACE WITHIN THE ROOM AT NO MORE
THAN .5 X ACTUAL ACTIVITY SPACE.
2.
ACTIVITY SPACE IS NOT LESS THAN 20’ IN SMALLEST DIMENSION
AND AT LEAST 25% OR 250 SQUARE FEET OF THIS SPACE
WHICHEVER IS GREATER IS PROVIDED WITH APPROVED EXERCISE
EQUIPMENT.
3.
SEE ARCHITECTURAL FLOOR PLANS FOR OVERALL RECREATION
BUILDING SPACE LAYOUT AND ALLOCATION OF RESOURCES.
OUTDOOR EATING AREA
1.
AREA CONSISTS OF EATING TABLES INCLUDING SEATS, GRILLS,
POTABLE WATER (SINKS) , TRASH/RECYCLING FEATURES BUILD
INTO CABINETRY, AND CIRCULATION AREA.
2.
OF AT LEAST 1 SQUARE FOOT PLUS 1 SF PER 10 EATING TABLE
SEATS, TRASH AND RECYCLING CONTAINERS AND POTABLE
WATER FOR EACH AREA.
3.
GRILLING DOES NOT REQUIRE A COAL BIN.
4.
ALL FEATURES ARE FIXED IN PLACE.
5.
ALL TABLES ARE WITHIN 50’ OF GRILLING AREA & NOT SEPARATED
BY GATES.
6.
AT LEAST 50% OF THE EATING TABLES ARE DESIGNED TO INCLUDE
PROVISIONS FOR SUN PROTECTION (BUILDINGS AND SHADE
TRELLIS). SEE SHEET G0.05 FOR SHADE STUDY.
OUTDOOR SEATING AREA
1.
SEATING AREA INCLUDES SEAT WALLS, FIXED CHAIRS AND FIXED
LOUNGERS.  NO PICNIC TABLES ARE PROVIDED.
2.
AT LEAST 50% OF THE EATING TABLES ARE DESIGNED TO INCLUDE
PROVISIONS FOR SUN PROTECTION (BUILDINGS, TREES, AND
SHADE TRELLIS). SEE SHEETS G0.04 AND G0.05 FOR SHADE
STUDIES.
GARDEN PLOTS
1.
ALL PLANT BEDS ARE A 12” MINIMUM HEIGHT RAISED AND RETAINED
PLANTING BEDS WITH IMPORT TOPSOIL SCREENED FREE OF
ROCKS. SIZE IS 24" X 5'. ALL SIZES ARE EQUAL.
2.
 WORK BENCH IS 5’ LONG X 2.5’ WIDE. 1 PER AREA.
3.
GROUND FLOOR TOOL LOCKER WILL BE A SPACE DEDICATED
INSIDE THE BUILDING. SEE ARCHITECTURAL PLANS. ROOF TOOL
LOCKER IS FREESTANDING: 6’ TALL X 1’ DEEP X 3’ WIDE.
4.
MULCH BIN/AREA IS 4’ X 5’.
5.
ONE TRASH CONTAINER IS PROVIDED PER AREA.
6.
HOSE BIB(S) WILL BE PROVIDED AS PART OF THE IRRIGATION
SYSTEM WITH EACH BED GROUPING HAVING A DEDICATED HOSE
BIB.
7.
THE GARDEN PLOTS RECEIVE A MINIMUM OF 3 HOURS OF FULL SUN
DURING THE HOURS OF 9 AM TO 5PM AT THE MARCH EQUINOX AND
SEPTEMBER EQUINOX. SEE SHEETS G0.04 AND G0.05 FOR SUN
STUDIES.
TABLE TENNIS
1.
TABLE TENNIS HAS REGULATION SIZE TABLE MEASURING 5’ WIDE
AND 9’ LONG AND REQUIRED UNIMPEDED PLAYABLE SPACE OF 11’ X
17’ FEET LONG.

1.
THE MAXIMUM ALLOWABLE SOIL WEIGHT FOR SOILS PLACED ON-STRUCTURE FOR THIS PROJECT IS 100 LBS/C.F.
SATURATED.
2.
ALL PLANTING AREAS TO BE IRRIGATED USING FULLY AUTOMATED DRIP IRRIGATION.
3.
PROVIDE 3-INCH DEPTH ORGANIC COMPOST MULCH AT ALL PLANTING AREAS, EXCEPT WHERE NOTED.
4.
WITHIN THE TRAFFIC SAFETY VISIBILITY TRIANGLES, ALL PLANTINGS (SHRUBS, BUSHES OR HEDGES) SHALL
MAINTAIN 3' MAXIMUM HEIGHT AND TREES SHALL HAVE 7' MIN. CLEAR TREE CANOPY PER THE CITY OF SAN MATEO
TRAFFIC SAFETY VISIBILITY AREA DESIGN GUIDELINES AND SIDE STREET/DRIVEWAY TRIANGLE OF SAFETY DESIGN
GUIDELINES.
5.
STREET TREES SHALL BE PLANTED A MINIMUM OF 10' FROM SANITARY SEWER LINES AND 5' FROM WATER LINES,
FIRE LINES, AND DRIVEWAYS.
GENERAL NOTES
1.
A MINIMUM 3” LAYER OF MULCH SHALL BE APPLIED ON ALL EXPOSED SOIL SURFACES OF PLANTING AREAS IN
ORDER TO PREVENT EVAPORATIVE WATER LOSS FROM EXPOSED SOIL, EXCEPT IN AREAS OF DIRECT SEEDING
APPLICATION (E.G., HYDROSEED).
2.
ORGANIC MULCH MATERIALS MADE FROM RECYCLED OR POSTCONSUMER SHALL TAKE PRECEDENCE OVER
INORGANIC MATERIALS OR VIRGIN FOREST PROJECTS UNLESS THE RECYCLED POSTCONSUMER ORGANIC
PRODUCTS ARE NOT LOCALLY AVAILABLE. ORGANIC MULCHES ARE NOT REQUIRED WHERE PROHIBITED BY LOCAL
FUEL MODIFICATION PLAN GUIDELINES OR OTHER APPLICABLE LOCAL ORDINANCES.
3.
PRIOR TO THE PLANTING OF ANY MATERIALS, COMPACTED SOILS SHALL BE TRANSFORMED TO A FRIABLE
CONDITION. ON ENGINEERED SLOPES, ONLY AMENDED PLANTING HOLES NEED MEET THIS REQUIREMENT.
4.
FOR LANDSCAPE INSTALLATIONS, COMPOST AT A RATE OF A MINIMUM OF FOUR CUBIC YARDS PER 1,000 SQUARE
FEET OF PERMEABLE AREA SHALL BE INCORPORATED TO A DEPTH OF 6” INTO THE SOIL. SOILS WITH GREATER
THAN 6 PERCENT ORGANIC MATTER IN THE TOP 6” OF SOIL ARE EXEMPT FROM ADDING COMPOST AND TILLING.
WATER CONSERVATION IN LANDSCAPING REGULATIONS NOTES

1.
CHUTE INTAKE VESTIBULES SHALL BE 2HR FIRE-RATED WITH 90-MINUTE FIRE-RATED ACCESS DOOR FOR RESIDENTIAL ACCESS. **NOTE THAT WHERE CHUTE INTAKE ROOMS ARE
PROTECTED BY AUTOMATIC SPRINKLERS, THE ROOM SHALL BE ENCLOSED IN A MIN OF 1HR FIRE RESISTANCE-RATED CONSTRUCTION WITH 45-MINUTE FIRE-RATED ACCESS DOORS**. 5'-0"
MIN DIAMETER WHEELCHAIR TURNING SPACE REQUIRED PER ADA REQUIREMENTS. POWER TO INTAKE DOORS SUPPLIED BY MCP. PROVIDE (2) 15x18 BOTTOM HINGED, LOW-VOLTAGE,
ELECTRICALLY INTERLOCKED, AUTOMATIC OPENING DOOR AT EACH FLOOR. SEE DETAIL 2/TR2.0. 30" x 48" FRONT / SIDE APPROACH REQUIRED PER ADA STANDARDS.
2.
MANAGEMENT TO PROVIDE 23-GALLON 'RUBBERMAID SLIM JIM' CONTAINER OR EQUIVALENT FOR COMPOST DISPOSAL. STAFF TO EMPTY IN CONTAINERS DAILY AT TRASH ROOM.
3.
2HR FIRE-RATED FACE WALL SHALL NOT BE ERECTED UNTIL CHUTES HAVE BEEN INSTALLED. FOR SOUND PROOFING PURPOSES, ATM RECOMMENDS DOUBLE STUD-WALLS OR
EQUIVALENT ADJACENT TO OCCUPIED SPACES. ATM RECOMMENDS INTERIOR OF SHAFT TO BE TAPED TO PREVENT ODOROUS AIR LEAKING INTO OCCUPIED SPACES. ARCHITECT TO
SELECT SUITABLE ASSEMBLY.
4.
TYPE I FLOOR: TO PREVENT CONCRETE BREAK-OFF, VERIFY MINIMUM DISTANCE WITH STRUCTURAL ENGINEER.
5.
ARCHITECT SHALL VERIFY ALL FLOOR SUPPORT FRAME ANCHORING CONNECTIONS WITH RECOMMENDATIONS IN ACOUSTICS REPORT.

The waivers to the following standards have been identified, to be applied pursuant to State Density Bonus 
Law:
a.
Floor Area and a Floor Area Ratio – For the C3-2 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.34.050(b), 
the FAR limit is 2.0. The project would result in an FAR of 3.9.
b.
Floor Area and a Floor Area Ratio – For the E2-1.5 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.48.060(c), 
the FAR limit is 1.5. The project would result in an FAR of 3.9. 
c.
Residential Density – The San Mateo General Plan 2040 Land Use Designation for this site is Residential 
Medium II, and the maximum base density is 99 dwellings per acre. For this 1.22-acre site, the 
maximum density is 120.7 dwellings. The proposed Project would include 181 dwelling units, exceeding 
the maximum density. However, the Project would reserve 15% of the base density (19 dwellings, or 
15.7% of the General Plan maximum) for Very-Low Income (VLI) households. Per Government Code 
section 65915(f)(2), a project with at least 15% of the dwellings reserved for VLI households is eligible 
for a density bonus of 50% of the base density. The 50% bonus applied to this site would increase the 
maximum allowable density to 182 dwellings (the General Plan density for this site is 120.7 dwellings, 
and per Government Code section 65915(q), the density is rounded up to 121 dwellings. The 50% 
bonus, when applied to this density, would allow 181.5 dwellings, and per Government Code section 
65915(q), the total number of dwellings allowed for this site is rounded up to 182 dwellings). While this 
Project would be eligible for a density increase to accommodate up to 182 dwellings, it proposes only 
181.
d.
Yards – For the E2-1.5 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.48.090, the yard along each street 
frontage must be at least 7.5 feet. The project would not provide a yard along North San Mateo Drive 
or Villa Terrace.
e.
Buffers-Rear yard – For the C3-2 portion of the site, per SMMC sections 27.34.060, 27.30.060(a) & 
27.22.080(c), the minimum yard is 25 feet along the portion of the site that abuts the R-zoned property. 
The project would provide a 2-foot yard abutting the R-zoned property.
f.
Buffer-Landscape – For the E2-1.5 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.48.100, a landscape buffer 
of at least one-half the height of the proposed building (or approx. 38 feet) must be provided along 
Villa Terrace and for the portion of the site that abuts the R-zoned property. The project would not 
provide a landscape buffer along Villa Terrace and would provide a 2-foot buffer, with landscaping to 
be provided via hanging vines, abutting the adjacent R-zoned property. 
g.
Parcel Coverage-Open Space – For the E2-1.5 portion of the site, per SMMC section 27.48.065, at-grade 
open space must be at least 20% of the parcel area. The project would not provide at-grade open space.
h.
Blank Walls – Per ODS section 4.1.1, “Blank walls shall be limited to a maximum of twenty (20) feet in 
length on all stories”. The ground-floor wall facing the residential district to the southwest would be 
over 10 feet in height (13 feet to 21 feet is proposed), the horizontal length would be greater than 20 
feet (326 linear feet is proposed), and the ground-floor wall would not include a transparent window 
or door.

residential, commercial, or other projects as defined. Therefore, the 325-space parking minimum 
established in SMMC section 27.64.160 is not applicable to the proposed project, and the City cannot 
require any parking. Nonetheless, the Project includes a total of 180 on-site parking spaces, which are 
provided voluntarily.

RE: 
PA25031 Application Resubmittal – 715 N. San Mateo Drive 
Dear Mr. Dahl, 
Prometheus Real Estate Group respectfully submits this Project Description Letter and associated 
materials in response to the City’s May 15 incompleteness letter regarding with the Project proposal 
located at 715 San Mateo Drive – PA-2025-031.  This letter modifies our July 15, 2025 formal 
application submittal correspondence to you 
 
The Project’s pre-application was submitted pursuant to SB 330, which amended the Housing 
Accountability Act (Gov. Code § 65889.5), the Permit Streamlining Act (Gov. Code § 65920 et seq.), and 
created the Housing Crisis Act of 2019 (Gov. Code § 66300).  The full application was timely submitted 
to preserve the vesting secured by the pre-application, as is this resubmittal. 
 
The SB330 Project application is consistent with the policies and guidelines of the adopted San Mateo 
General Plan 2040 in proposing a 181-unit residential development. It will allow an aging vehicle sales 
center and parking lot to convert to much needed market rate and affordable rental housing within 
walking distance to Downtown San Mateo and Caltrain. 
 
We believe that this request is fully consistent with San Mateo’s vision and goals of providing housing 
opportunities in focused areas of San Mateo as guided by the recently adopted General Plan. This 1.22-
acre site is situated within the San Mateo Drive high residential corridor between downtown San Mateo 
and Downtown Burlingame. This proposal supports guiding language of the San Mateo General Plan to 
“Encourage new development to maximize the density and intensity specified in the Land Use Plan and to 
efficiently use land and infrastructure resources” and, ”provide a range of housing types, sizes, and 
affordability levels in all San Mateo neighborhoods” (Policy LU 1.3).” Accompanying this Project 
Description Letter are the required Project plans and application documents. 
 
Moreover, we believe that the Project satisfies the requirements for a statutory CEQA exemption 
pursuant to AB 130, which went into effect on July 1.  We will provide Staff with a detailed analysis that 
supports this contention shortly. 
 
 
I. 
Project Description 
 
The Project will consist of six stories of residential units comprised of studio, one-bedroom, two- 
bedroom, and three-bedroom units over an internal and partially underground parking garage, the 
entrance of which will be visually minimized per General Plan Policy CD 7.4. The upper floors of 
residential units are oriented around a southern facing courtyard and include a pool, spa, BBQ,

--- page 149 ---
planting, and seating options. An amenity space on the 6th floor will provide a gathering space for the 
residents.   The Southwestern end of the courtyard will be anchored by the pool area surrounded by 
seating and adjacent to a gym for residents of the building. 
 
In keeping with General Plan Policy CD 7.3, the Project design enhances the neighborhood’s visual and 
architectural character by providing high-quality materials and construction, open space, and resident 
amenities, while providing much needed housing, this carefully considered design draws upon the 
immediate neighborhood context and the broader regional vernacular for design cues and inspiration 
that honor the midrise elements of San Mateo’s Multifamily Objective Design Standards (ODS), Action 
CD 7.7. Soft creamy stucco, brick (two tones), wood-appearance cladding and ironwork (per ODS 4.1.3) 
connect with the Mediterranean tradition in San Mateo architecture, while updating with 
contemporary forms.  The project intends to comply with the Public Art requirement by paying an in-
lieu fee. 
 
The street facades present refined solidity with deep carving, stepping and variation and a general 
rhythm of thirds per ODS 4.1.4, 4.1.6B1 and 4.1.6C.  The design presents a clear high-bay base with 
brick cladding per ODS4.1.6A1 and 4.1.6.B2C.  The base has deep set openings, ground floor units, 
active uses and space for planting for an inviting pedestrian experience.  At podium level, a linear 
courtyard extends through the massing with active balconies, walkways and biophilic elements.  The 
southwest corner of the building is carved back in reference to the massing context of adjacent 
neighboring buildings per ODS4.4.1B.  Facades are articulated with balconies and window recessed per 
ODS 4.1.2 B&D. The vehicular driveway is positioned on Villa Terrace per ODS 3.2.3 and all parking is 
shielded from the street and wrapped in program.  
 
II. 
Density Bonus Law 
 
The Project incorporates the use of the State Density Bonus Law (Gov. Code § 65915 [“DBL”]). The DBL 
has four distinct primary components: (1) Density Bonuses; (2) Incentives; (3) Development Standard 
Waivers; and (4) Parking Standard Waivers. Although interrelated, each component serves a different 
purpose and is governed by unique standards.  
A. 
Density Bonus 
 
Section 65915(b)(1) of the DBL provides that requests for a density bonus must be granted “when an 
applicant for a housing development seeks and agrees to construct a housing development” that meets 
one or more of the statute’s thresholds, including at least 5% of the units for Very Low Income 
households. 
 
The Project is located within the Residential Medium II land use designation of the San Mateo General 
Plan, which allows a maximum of 99 du/ac, and which equates to a maximum residential density of 121 
units on the project site. The Project implements the DBL to include 15% Very Low Income units (19 
total) and therefore receives a 50% density bonus (60 Units), which equates to a total unit count of 181 
Units. (Gov. Code § 65915(f)(2).   
 
B. 
Incentives 
A local agency must grant an incentive request unless it can make a written finding, based on substantial 
evidence, that: (1) the incentive does not result in identifiable and actual cost reductions to provide for 
affordable housing costs; (2) the incentive would have a specific, adverse impact on the public health or

--- page 150 ---
safety, or upon an historical resource; or (3) would be contrary to state or federal law. (Gov. Code 
§ 65915(d)(1).) We submit that none of those findings can be made with regard to this project. 
Recent case law confirms that an applicant is not required to establish that the requested incentive will 
result in cost reductions. In Schreiber v. City of Los Angeles (2021) 69 Cal.App.5th 549, 555, the court 
explained that there is a presumption that an incentive will result in cost reductions and that an 
applicant “is not required to establish that cost reductions will result.” Instead, a city must approve the 
incentive request unless it makes one of the written findings set forth in Section 65915(d)(1) above. 
(Ibid.) “By requiring the city to grant incentives unless it makes particular findings, the statute places the 
burden of proof on the city to overcome the presumption that incentives will result in cost reductions.” 
(Id. at 556.) Because of this presumption, a city is “not required to make an affirmative finding that the 
incentives would result in cost reductions, or to cite evidence to establish a fact presumed to be true.” 
(Id. at 560.) 
 
The number of incentives is derived from the amount of affordable units that are provided. In this case, 
by providing at least 15% of the units for VLI households, the Project applicant may receive three 
incentives. (Gov. Code (§ 65915(d)(2)(C).) This Project Application does not identify the use of any 
Incentives at this time.  However, we reserve our right to identify and seek the three incentives 
available in response to feedback from City staff during the entitlement process. 
 
C. 
Development Standard Waivers 
 
In addition to, and separate from, requests for incentives, a DBL applicant may request a waiver or 
reduction of development standards that would have the effect of physically precluding the construction 
of the project proposed by the developer. (Gov. Code § 65915(e)(1).) The definition of a “development 
standard” includes a site or construction condition, including, without limitation, local height, setback, 
floor area ratio, onsite open space, and parking area ratio requirements that would otherwise apply to 
residential development pursuant to ordinances, general plan elements, specific plans, charters, or 
other local condition, law, policy, resolution, or regulation. (Gov. Code § 65915(o)(1).) A request for a 
development standard waiver neither reduces nor increases the number of incentives to which the 
developer is otherwise entitled. (Gov. Code § 65915(e)(2).) Furthermore, there is no limit on the 
number of waivers that may be issued. 
As with incentives, recent case law has clarified the legal principles regarding waivers. The Schreiber 
case confirms that a city may refuse a request to waive or reduce development standards only if it 
makes written findings that the waiver or reduction would have a specific adverse impact on the public 
health or safety. (Id. at 556; Gov. Code § 65915(e)(1).) In addition, another new case upholding a city’s 
approval of a DBL project confirmed that waivers are based on the project as proposed by the 
developer: “even if we assume the Project as designed is inconsistent with some of the City’s design 
standards, the Density Bonus Law would preclude the City from applying those standards to deny this 
project.” (Bankers Hill 150 v. City of San Diego (2022) 74 Cal.App.5th 755, 775.) Therefore, a local agency 
may not respond to a waiver request that a Project could be redesigned to avoid the need for a waiver. 
(Id. at 774-775 [rejecting argument that the Project “could have been built more horizontally” to comply 
with design standards.”].)  In addition, HCD has notified various local agencies that they cannot require a 
qualifying DBL project to be redesigned in order to avoid the need for a waiver.  Last year, HCD advised 
the City of Oceanside as follows: “HCD reminds the City that appellate courts have established (and 
continue to affirm) that local agencies cannot lawfully redesign a qualifying SDBL project on the theory 
that if the project were configured differently, it would not need the requested incentives/concessions 
and waivers. (Wollmer v. City of Berkeley (2011) 193 Cal.App.4th 1329, 1346–1347.)  The City must

--- page 151 ---
consider the Project as proposed, inclusive of any requested concessions or waivers.”1   
 
 
At this point, we identify the following waivers or reductions to the development standards identified 
below: 
•

not provided.

Subject: 
Applicability of AB 130 CEQA Exemption to the Ford Site/715 N. San Mateo 
Drive, San Mateo Project, PA-2025-031 
On June 30, 2025, a new statutory CEQA exemption for multifamily housing development 
projects was enacted as part of Assembly Bill 130 (“AB 130”) and became effective immediately. 
(See Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66.) The new AB 130 statutory CEQA exemption is similar to the 
existing categorical Class 32 exemption under the CEQA Guidelines, except that AB 130: 1) 
accommodates larger residential projects; 2) reduces legal risks by limiting opportunity for third party 
challenges (no “unusual circumstances” challenges are permitted); and 3) creates a strict project 
approval timeline starting with application completeness. 
This memorandum reviews the application materials for the 715 N. San Mateo Drive Project 
(“Project”) proposed at 715 N. San Mateo Dr., San Mateo, California (“Property”) to determine the 
applicability of the new AB 130 CEQA exemption to the Project. Additionally, this memorandum 
briefly outlines how the streamlined approval timeline will impact the Project. We note that unlike 
the Class 32 Exemption, an analysis of potential impacts related to traffic, noise, air quality, and 
water quality will not be required to support the exemption. Instead, the project site must meet all of 
the SB 35 siting criteria (see below). Therefore, qualifying housing development projects should be 
processed much more quickly since technical studies should not be required, with the possible 
exception of a desktop biological resources survey.  
 As we explain below, the Project qualifies for the AB 130 CEQA exemption. We recommend 
that this memorandum be shared with the City of San Mateo (“City”) before the Project application is 
deemed complete (or Prometheus notifies the City that it qualifies for AB 130) so that the City will 
be in a position to timely initiate the mandatory tribal consultation process, discussed in Section II 
below.

--- page 154 ---
To: Prometheus Real Estate Group 
From: David H. Blackwell 
Date:  August 11, 2025 
Page 2 
 
 
4917-2528-5210.3/  
372819-00030/8-11-25/dhb/dhb 
 
 
 
I. 
NEW CEQA EXEMPTION ELIGIBILITY REQUIREMENTS 
To qualify for the AB 130 CEQA exemption, the project must satisfy specific site and project 
requirements. Unlike other housing streamlining laws enacted in recent years, AB 130 does not 
contain any affordability requirements, and labor requirements are limited to only a narrow class of 
projects, none of which fit the description for the Project. As described below, the Project fits each of 
the AB 130 qualifying criteria. 
a. Housing project. The project must be a housing development project, which is 
defined to include: (1) projects consisting of residential uses only; (2) mixed-use 
projects where at least two-thirds of the new or converted square footage is designated 
for residential use; (3) mixed-use projects with greater than 500 units where at least 
half of the new or converted square footage is designated for residential use and other 
specific requirements are met; (4) transitional housing or supportive housing; and (5) 
farmworker housing. (Gov. Code §§ 65589.5(h)(2), 65905.5(b); Pub. Res. Code 
§ 21080.66(a).)  
The Project meets this requirement because it will be developed with 100% residential 
uses. 
b. Acreage. The project site must be 20 acres or less, except Builder’s Remedy project 
sites must be 5 acres or less. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(a)(1).) 
The Project meets this requirement because it is not a Builder’s Remedy project and 
the Property is 1.22 acres. 
c. Urban area. The project site must be within the boundaries of an incorporated 
municipality or in an urban area, as defined by the U.S. Census Bureau. (Pub. Res. 
Code § 21080.66(a)(2).) 
The Project meets this requirement because it is within the City of San Mateo, an 
incorporated municipality. 
d. Infill location. The project site must be an urban infill site, meaning that: (i) the site 
was previously developed with an urban use; (ii) at least 75% of the perimeter of the 
site adjoins parcels that are developed with urban uses; (iii) at least 75% of the area 
within a one-quarter mile radius of the site is developed with urban uses; or (iv) for 
sites with four sides, at least three sides are developed with urban uses and at least

--- page 155 ---
To: Prometheus Real Estate Group 
From: David H. Blackwell 
Date:  August 11, 2025 
Page 3 
 
 
4917-2528-5210.3/  
372819-00030/8-11-25/dhb/dhb 
 
 
two-thirds of the perimeter of the site adjoins parcels that are developed with urban 
uses. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(a)(3).) 
The Project meets this requirement because the Property is currently developed with a 
vehicular sales center and residence, which qualify as “urban uses.” The Property 
also qualifies under the other definitions of urban infill site because it is surrounded 
on at least 75% of the perimeter, or three of four sides, by urban uses. 
e. Environmental siting criteria. The project must meet environmental siting criteria 
set forth in SB 35/423. To qualify, a site must not be located in any of the following: 
1) certain areas of the coastal zone; 2) prime farmland, farmland of statewide 
importance, or land designated for agricultural protection or preservation; 3) wetlands; 
4) a very high fire hazard severity zone (unless certain mitigation measures adopted); 
5) a hazardous waste site; 6) a delineated earthquake fault zone; 7) a 100-year flood 
hazard area or regulatory floodway; 8) lands identified for conservation or under a 
conservation easement; or 9) habitat for protected species. (Pub. Res. Code 
§ 21080.66(a)(6); Gov. Code § 65913.4(a)(6).) 
The Project meets this requirement because the Property does not fall within any of 
the prohibited categories. Specifically: 
i. The Property is not within the coastal zone; 
ii. The Property is not on land used or designated for agriculture; 
iii. The Property is not on a wetland; 
iv. The Property is not within a very high fire hazard severity zone, per our review 
of the Office of the State Fire Marshal’s Fire Hazard Severity Zone maps; 
v. The Property is not on a hazardous waste site, per our review of the Cortese 
List of hazardous waste sites; 
vi. The Property is not within a delineated earthquake fault zone, per our review 
of the California Department of Conservation’s Earthquake Hazards Zone 
Application; 
vii. The Property is not within a 100-year flood hazard area nor a regulatory

f. Land use regulations. The project must be consistent with the applicable general plan 
and zoning ordinance, as well as any applicable local coastal program. If the general 
plan and zoning ordinance are inconsistent, the project need only be consistent with 
one. Use of any State Density Bonus Law density bonus, incentive or concession, 
waiver, or reduced parking ratio shall not be grounds to determine the project is 
inconsistent with the zoning, general plan, or local coastal program. The housing 
development shall be deemed consistent if there is substantial evidence that would 
allow a reasonable person to conclude as such. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(a)(4).) 
The Project meets this requirement because it is consistent with the land use 
designations for the Property. The Property is designated “Residential Medium II” in 
the City’s 2040 General Plan and is within the Executive Office (“E2-1.5”) zoning 
district. The Residential Medium II designation permits residential uses, with a 
maximum density range of 51 – 99 dwelling units per acre. The E2-1.5 zoning district 
permits residential uses subject to R3 district minimum development standards. 
Because the Property is over 50,000 square feet, those standards require a minimum 
1,250 square feet of parcel area per dwelling unit, or roughly 42 dwelling units per 
acre. This is inconsistent with the minimum density of the Residential Medium II 
general plan designation. Under AB 130, if the general plan and zoning are 
inconsistent, then the Project shall be deemed consistent with both if it is consistent 
with one. 
Per the Project application, the residential density will be 99 dwelling units per acre 
which is within the General Plan range for the Property. Further, because the Project 
qualifies for a density bonus, any development standards that would preclude 
development of the Project as designed, such as the minimum parcel area per dwelling 
unit standard, will be waived or reduced. 
g. Minimum density. The proposed residential density must be at least 50% of the 
minimum residential density deemed appropriate to accommodate housing for the 
jurisdiction. Depending on the type of jurisdiction (nonmetropolitan, suburban, or 
metropolitan), the minimum density ranges from 5 to 15 units per acre. (Gov. Code § 
65583.2(c)(3)(B); Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(a)(5).)

II. 
NEW PROJECT APPROVAL TIMELINE 
AB 130 also amended the Permit Streamlining Act (“PSA”) to create a new approval timeline 
for agencies with approval authority over projects that qualify for the AB 130 CEQA exemption. 
(Gov. Code § 65950(a)(7).) The amended PSA states that an agency must approve or disapprove the 
project “[t]hirty days from the conclusion of [the tribal consultation process]” for projects invoking 
the new CEQA exemption. (Id.)

--- page 159 ---
To: Prometheus Real Estate Group 
From: David H. Blackwell 
Date:  August 11, 2025 
Page 7 
 
 
4917-2528-5210.3/  
372819-00030/8-11-25/dhb/dhb 
 
 
Additionally, the tribal consultation process itself contains statutory approval timelines that, 
when combined with the new PSA provisions, establish a single approval timeline for an AB 130 
project starting with application completeness, or for applications already deemed complete, when 
the applicant notifies the City that the project qualifies for AB 130. Because the tribal consultation 
process can conclude in multiple ways, the exact timing cannot be determined from the outset. At a 
minimum, if no tribes elect to participate in the consultation, a project must be approved no later than 
104 days from the date of application completeness/AB 130 notification. If a tribe elects to 
participate in the consultation, a project must be approved no later than 178 days from the date of 
application completeness/AB 130 notification, but may be approved earlier.  
At this time, we understand the Project’s application is under review with the City Planning 
Department. Under AB 130, the approval timeline begins either when the application is deemed 
complete, or for projects with already completed applications, when the applicant notifies the City 
that the project qualifies for AB 130. (Gov. Code § 21080.66(b)(1)(A)(i)-(ii); § 65589.5(h)(5).) For 
the purposes of AB 130, “deemed complete” means the applicant has submitted an SB 330 
preliminary application. (Id.) Therefore, if a preliminary application was previously submitted for the 
Project, Prometheus can start the approval timeline immediately by notifying the City that the Project 
qualifies for AB 130. Note that the City only has 14 days from the date of application 
completeness/AB 130 notification to provide formal notification to tribes. Therefore, we recommend 
informing the City as soon as possible that the Project will utilize the AB 130 CEQA exemption to 
ensure that there are no delays once the application is deemed complete or Prometheus makes an AB 
130 notification. As stated above, at least one tribe participated in the preparation of the 2024 General 
Plan, so it is possible that the Project may go through this consultation process.

Executive Summary 
This report presents the results of the local transportation analysis conducted for the residential 
development proposed at 715 North San Mateo Drive in San Mateo, California. The site consists of four 
parcels (APNs 032-151-130, -160, -300, -320) along the south side of San Mateo Drive, with frontage 
along State Street, San Mateo Drive, and Villa Terrace. The project proposes to demolish two existing 
vacant commercial buildings and parking lots formerly used as car dealerships and a single family 
detached house and construct a 6-story residential building consisting of 181 residential units 
(consisting of 162 market-rate units and 19 below market-rate units for very-low income households). A 
parking garage would be located on the first floor and the basement level. Vehicle access to the parking 
garage would be provided by a single full-access driveway located along Villa Terrace. 
This study evaluates potential local transportation effects of the project in accordance with the 
standards set forth by the City of San Mateo.  
Project Trip Estimates 
The Institute of Transportation Engineers’ (ITE) Trip Generation Manual, 12th Edition, was used to 
estimate the vehicle trips that would be generated by the project. After applying the appropriate ITE trip 
generation rate, the proposed project is estimated to generate a gross of 807 daily trips, with 69 trips 
(16 inbound and 53 outbound) during the AM peak hour and 69 trips (44 inbound and 25 outbound) 
during the PM peak hour. 
Intersection Level of Service Analysis 
The results of the intersection level of service analysis (see Table ES-1) show that all study 
intersections would operate at an acceptable level of service with and without the addition of project 
trips under all evaluated scenarios. 
Other Transportation Issues 
Traffic associated with the project would not contribute to any increase in vehicle queues at any of the 
studied intersections. The proposed site plan shows that the project would provide generally adequate 
site access and on-site circulation, and would not interfere with pedestrian, bicycle, or transit circulation 
in the area. The project is not subject to any minimum vehicular parking requirements and would 
provide adequate bicycle parking. The project should consider the following recommendations resulting 
from the site plan review:

--- page 163 ---
715 North San Mateo Drive Residential LTA 
March 5, 2026 
P a g e  |  i i  
Recommendations 
• 
The security gate at the driveway should be installed approximately 30 feet from the sidewalk in 
order to minimize the effect of queueing on the sidewalk and traffic operations on Villa Terrace.  
• 
Appropriate visual and/or audible warning signals should be provided at the project driveway to 
alert pedestrians of vehicles exiting the driveway. 
• 
Landscaping near the driveway and intersection corners should be placed and maintained such 
that it does not interfere with sight distance. Trees should have a high canopy of at least 6 feet 
and other landscaping should be kept at a low level below 3 feet.  
• 
Landscaping provided at corners should be less than 3 feet tall at the corner to maintain the 
required sight distance. 
• 
Each tandem parking space and adjacent parking should be assigned to the same unit.

1.  
Introduction 
This report presents the results of the local transportation analysis conducted for the residential 
development proposed at 715 North San Mateo Drive in San Mateo, California (see Figures 1 and 2). 
The site consists of four parcels (APNs 032-151-130, -160, -300, -320) along the south side of San 
Mateo Drive, with frontage along State Street, San Mateo Drive, and Villa Terrace. The project 
proposes to demolish two existing vacant commercial buildings and parking lots formerly used as car 
dealerships and a single family detached house and construct a 6-story residential building consisting 
of 181 residential units (consisting of 162 market-rate units and 19 below market-rate units for very-low 
income households). A parking garage would be located on the first floor and the basement level. 
Vehicle access to the parking garage would be provided by a single full-access driveway located along 
Villa Terrace. 
Scope of Study 
The purpose of this study is to identify potential local transportation effects of the project in accordance 
with standards and methodologies set forth by the City of San Mateo. 
Local Transportation Analysis (LTA) 
The City of San Mateo requires projects to measure intersection operations and to provide 
improvements or address project related operational deficiencies through a Local Transportation 
Analysis (LTA). The LTA also includes an evaluation of the project’s effect on transit, bicycle, and 
pedestrian access, a review of site access and circulation, and a parking analysis. 
This study analyzes the traffic effects of the project on the key intersections in the vicinity of the site 
during the weekday AM and PM peak hours of traffic. The weekday AM peak hour is generally between 
7:00 AM and 9:00 AM and the weekday PM peak hour is generally between 4:00 PM and 6:00 PM. On 
a typical weekday (Tuesday through Thursday), these are the periods when the most congested traffic 
generally occurs. 
This study includes an analysis of the weekday peak-hour traffic conditions of three intersections, as 
listed below, in accordance with the City’s TIA guidelines. 
Study Intersections 
1. San Mateo Drive and Villa Terrace 
2. Highland Avenue and Villa Terrace 
3. Project Driveway and Villa Terrace

Intersection traffic conditions were evaluated for the following scenarios: 
• 
Existing Conditions. Existing AM and PM peak-hour traffic volumes were obtained from new 
turning-movement counts conducted on October 30, 2025. Traffic counts are included in 
Appendix A. 
• 
Opening Year Plus Project Conditions. Per the City of San Mateo’s development project 
database, accessed November 18, 2025, there are no approved developments near the project 
site that would be expected to add traffic to the study intersections. Thus, the opening year plus 
project conditions were estimated by adding the new traffic estimated to be generated by the 
project to existing traffic volumes. Intersection effects associated with the development would be 
evaluated relative to existing conditions.  
• 
Cumulative No Project Conditions. Cumulative traffic volumes represent traffic volumes and 
roadway conditions projected at the City’s General Plan Buildout in the year 2040. The City’s 
recently adopted General Plan did not produce intersection volume forecasts. Thus, cumulative 
traffic volumes were developed using the latest citywide travel demand model. 
• 
Cumulative Plus Project Conditions. Cumulative plus project traffic volumes were estimated 
by adding to the cumulative traffic volumes the new traffic generated by the project. Intersection 
effects associated with the development will be evaluated relative to cumulative conditions. 
Other Transportation Issues 
The study includes an evaluation of potential operational deficiencies related to transit services and a 
review of site access, on-site circulation, traffic calming, and parking. 
Intersection Operations Analysis Methodology 
This section presents the methods used to determine traffic conditions at the study intersections. It 
includes descriptions of the data requirements, the analysis methodologies, and the applicable level of 
service standards.

The data required for the analysis was obtained from traffic counts, the City of San Mateo, and field 
observations. The following data was collected: 
•

Intersection Level of Service Analysis Methodologies and Standards 
Traffic conditions at the study intersections were evaluated using level of service (LOS). Level of 
service is a qualitative description of operating conditions ranging from LOS A, or free-flow conditions 
with little or no delay, to LOS F, or jammed conditions with excessive delays. This study utilizes 
Synchro software to determine intersection levels of service based on the latest HCM methodology. 
Unsignalized Intersections  
Level of service analysis at unsignalized intersections is generally used to determine the need for 
modifications in the type of intersection control (i.e., all-way stop or signalization). As part of the 
evaluation, traffic volumes, delays and traffic signal warrants are evaluated to determine if the existing 
intersection control is appropriate.

--- page 169 ---
715 North San Mateo Drive Residential LTA 
March 5, 2026 
P a g e  |  5  
For unsignalized intersections, level of service depends on the average delay experienced by vehicles 
on the stop-controlled approaches. For side street stop-controlled intersections (two-way or T-
intersections), operations are defined by the average control delay experienced by vehicles entering the 
intersection from the stop-controlled approaches on minor streets or from left-turn approaches on major 
streets. The level of service is reported based on the average delay for the worst approach. The level of 
service definitions for unsignalized intersections are shown in Table 1.  
The City of San Mateo’s level of service standard for unsignalized intersections is LOS E. 
Table 1       
Unsignalized Intersection Level of Service Definitions Based on Average Delay  
 
Intersection Vehicle Queuing Analysis 
The analysis of intersection operations was supplemented with a vehicle queuing analysis at 
intersections where the project would add a substantial number of trips to the left-turn movements or 
stop-controlled approaches. The vehicle queuing analysis is used to determine the appropriate storage 
lengths for the high demand turn lanes where the project would add a substantial number of trips.  
An evaluation of vehicle queuing was conducted using the Synchro software, utilizing its estimate of the 
95th percentile number of queued vehicles and a comparison of this estimate to available storage space 
for the movement assuming 25 feet per vehicle.  
Definition of Adverse Intersection Operational Effects 
A local transportation analysis was conducted to evaluate the project’s consistency with the level of 
service standards set forth in the City’s guidelines and to identify feasible improvements to remedy 
deficiencies. Adverse operational effects at study intersections are based on the City of San Mateo 
standards.  
An adverse traffic operations issue is identified by the City for unsignalized intersections if the addition 
of traffic generated by the proposed project results in one of the following for either peak hour: 
1. The addition of project traffic causes the average intersection delay for all-way stop-controlled or 
the worst movement/approach for side-street stop-controlled intersections to degrade to LOS F,

If the operations of an unsignalized intersection become deficient based on LOS then an adverse effect

(CA MUTCD). If a project is near a school or downtown area with substantial pedestrian activity then 
City may require additional warrants to be evaluated such as pedestrian, accident history, etc.

This report has a total of five chapters. Chapter 2 describes the existing roadway network, transit 
service, bicycle and pedestrian facilities, and intersection levels of service. Chapter 3 presents the 
method used to estimate project traffic and the resulting intersection levels of service under opening

the resulting levels of service under cumulative no project and cumulative plus project conditions. 
Chapter 5 presents the analysis of other transportation-related issues, including intersection queuing, 
site access and circulation, parking, and effects to pedestrian, bicycle, and transit facilities.

2.  
Existing Transportation Conditions 
This chapter describes the existing conditions for transportation facilities in the vicinity of the site, 
including the roadway network, transit services, pedestrian and bicycle facilities, and traffic operations 
at the study intersections.  
Existing Roadway Network 
Regional access to the project site is provided via US 101 and El Camino Real (also known as State 
Route 82 or SR 82). Local access to the site is provided via San Mateo Drive, State Street, Highland 
Avenue, and Villa Terrace. These facilities are described below. 
US 101 is a north-south, ten-lane freeway (four mixed-flow lanes and one express lane in each 
direction) in the vicinity of the site. US 101 extends northward to San Francisco and southward to San 
Jose. Access to and from the site is provided by interchanges at Poplar Avenue for southbound US 101 
and at Airport Boulevard for northbound US 101. 
El Camino Real (SR 82) is a north-south highway with four lanes in the vicinity of the site. It is 
designated as a principal arterial per the City of San Mateo General Plan 2040. SR 82 extends from 
San Francisco to San Jose. Continuous sidewalks are provided on both sides of the street, with on-
street parking not being allowed in the project vicinity. In the project vicinity, the posted speed limit is 35 
miles per hour (mph). Access to and from the site is provided via State Street.  
San Mateo Drive is a north-south minor arterial per the General Plan. It has one lane in each direction 
and extends from 5th Avenue in the south to Peninsula Avenue in the north where it transitions into 
California Drive. It has a posted speed limit of 30 mph. On-street parking is allowed on both sides of the 
street. Continuous sidewalks are present on both sides of the street. There is a Class III bike route with 
sharrows on both sides of the street from 5th Avenue to Catalpa Street and Class II bike lanes on both 
sides of the street from Catalpa Street to Peninsula Avenue where it transitions back to a bike route. 
San Mateo Drive provides access to and from the project via Villa Terrace. 
State Street is an east-west local street per the General Plan. It has one lane in each direction and 
extends from San Mateo Drive in the east to El Camino Real in the west. It has a posted speed limit of 
25 mph. On-street parking is allowed on both sides of the street. Continuous sidewalks are present on 
both sides of the street. Access to the project is provided by Highland Avenue and San Mateo Drive. 
Highland Avenue is a north-south local street per the General Plan. It has one lane in each direction 
and extends from California Drive in the north to Santa Inez Avenue in the south. It has a posted speed 
limit of 25 mph. On-street parking is allowed on both sides of the street. Continuous sidewalks are 
present on both sides of the street. Access to and from the site is provided by Villa Terrace.

--- page 172 ---
715 North San Mateo Drive Residential LTA 
March 5, 2026 
P a g e  |  8  
Villa Terrace is an east-west local street per the General Plan. It has one lane in each direction and 
extends from Highland Avenue in the west to Claremont Street in the east. It has a posted speed limit 
of 25 mph. On-street parking is allowed on both sides of the street. Continuous sidewalks are present 
on both sides of the street. Villa Terrace provides direct site access through a proposed full-access 
driveway approximately 150 feet west of its intersection with San Mateo Drive. 
Existing Transit Services 
Existing public transit services in the study area are provided by SamTrans and Caltrain. SamTrans 
operates bus routes in San Mateo County, including routes ECR, 292, 46, 53/53P and 397 within 0.5 
miles of the project site. The nearest bus stop to the project site is located approximately 0.2 miles from 
the project site at the intersection of California Avenue/San Mateo Drive and Peninsula Avenue and is 
served by route 292. Caltrain provides commuter transit across the Bay Area from San Francisco to 
Gilroy, with the nearest station to the project site being the Burlingame station, located slightly over 0.5 
miles from the proposed main entrance to the project by foot. Public transit options in the vicinity of the 
site are shown in Table 2 and Figure 3.

Existing Pedestrian Facilities 
Pedestrian facilities consist of sidewalks and crosswalks. Sidewalks are present on all streets in the 
nearby project area. Crosswalks with pedestrian signal heads and push buttons are provided at all 
signalized intersections surrounding the site. 
Within 0.5 mile of the project site, curb ramps are present at all signalized intersections and most 
unsignalized intersections. Most corners meet current ADA curb ramp designs.  
The project site is located in a primarily residential area, with nearby commercial areas predominantly 
providing auto-related services. Downtown Burlingame and Downtown San Mateo are located 
approximately 11 minutes (0.5 miles) and 16 minutes (0.7miles) away by foot, respectively. These 
areas are accessible from the project site via sidewalks. 
Existing Bicycle Facilities 
The bicycle facilities that exist within a half mile of the project site (see Figure 4) include striped bike 
lanes (Class II bikeways), and bike routes (Class III bikeways). Class II bike lanes are lanes on 
roadways designated for use by bicycles with special lane markings, pavement legends, and signage. 
Class III bike routes are streets with signage and pavement markings where bicyclists share a travel 
lane with motorists. 
Bike facilities in the project area are described below: 
Bike Lane (Class II) 
• 
San Mateo Drive (from Peninsula Avenue to Catalpa Street) 
• 
Delaware Street (from Poplar Avenue to Indian Avenue) 
• 
Humboldt Street (from Peninsula Avenue to 9th Avenue) 
• 
Poplar Avenue (from El Camino Real to Claremont Street) 
• 
Howard Avenue (from Myrtle Road to Humboldt Street) 
Bike Route (Class III) 
• 
San Mateo Drive/California Drive (from Peninsula Avenue to Oak Grove Avenue) 
• 
Delaware Street (from Peninsula Avenue to 1st Avenue) 
• 
Monte Diablo Avenue (east of San Mateo Drive, connecting to the Bay Trail via a 
bicycle/pedestrian-only crossing over US-101) 
Existing Lane Configurations and Traffic Volumes 
The existing lane configurations at the study intersections were obtained from observations in the field. 
Existing peak-hour intersection volumes were obtained from turning movement counts collected on 
October 30, 2025, when nearby schools were in session, during typical peak traffic hours between 7:00 
AM and 9:00 AM and between 4:00 PM and 6:00 PM. Existing lane configurations and peak-hour 
intersection traffic volumes are shown in Figure 5. Traffic counts are presented in Appendix A. 
Existing Intersection Levels of Service 
The results of the intersection level of service analysis show that all of the study intersections are 
currently operating at acceptable levels of service (see Table 3). The intersection levels of service 
calculation sheets are included in Appendix C.

3.  
Opening Year Conditions 
This chapter presents opening year traffic conditions, which are defined as conditions just prior to 
completion of the project. Traffic volumes for opening year conditions comprise volumes from existing 
traffic counts plus traffic generated by approved but not yet constructed developments in the vicinity of 
the project site. This chapter describes the method for determining generated trips, the procedure used 
to determine opening year traffic volumes, and the resulting traffic conditions. 
Project Trip Estimates 
The magnitude of traffic produced by the new development and the locations where that traffic would 
appear were estimated using a three-step process: (1) trip generation, (2) trip distribution, and (3) trip 
assignment. In determining project trip generation, the magnitude of traffic entering and exiting the site 
is estimated for the AM and PM peak hours. As part of the project trip distribution, an estimate is made 
of the directions to and from which the project trips would travel. In the project trip assignment, the 
project trips are assigned to specific streets and intersections. These procedures are described below. 
Trip Generation 
Through empirical research, data have been collected that quantify the amount of traffic produced by 
many types of land uses. The research is compiled in the ITE Trip Generation Manual, 12th Edition. 
The magnitude of traffic added to the roadway system by a particular development is estimated by 
multiplying the applicable trip generation rates by the size of the development.  
The rate for “Multi-Family Housing (Mid-Rise) – Not Close to Rail Transit” (Land Use Code 221) was 
used to estimate trips generated by the proposed development. The Trip Generation Manual also 
provides rates for projects close to rail transit. Per the ITE manual, ‘a site is considered close to rail 
transit if the walking distance between the residential site entrance and the closest rail transit station 
entrance is ½ - mile or less.’ 
It is important to note that the methods used to measure distance from transit are different between the 
ITE Trip Generation Manual and the method used to measure distance between a project and a major 
transit stop under AB 2097 (whose parking requirement exemptions can be applied to this project as 
discussed in Chapter 5), which utilizes a straight line drawn from any point on the project’s parcel and 
the nearest edge of the parcel containing a major transit stop, and does not reference walking distance.  
The project’s main entrance would be approximately 0.52 miles by foot from the nearest point of the 
Burlingame Caltrain Station, and as such would be unable to apply the “close to rail transit” trip

--- page 179 ---
715 North San Mateo Drive Residential LTA 
March 5, 2026 
P a g e  |  1 5  
generation rate as the walking distance between the two is over 0.5 miles (see Figure 6). Furthermore, 
because the project would be on the borderline of eligibility, using the rate for sites not close to rail 
transit ensures a conservative analysis. 
The project site is currently vacant aside from one single-family detached house. As a conservative 
approach, no existing trip credits from the single family home were applied for the trip generation.  
Based on these trip rates, the project is estimated to generate a gross of 807 daily trips, with 69 trips 
(16 inbound and 53 outbound) during the AM peak hour and 69 trips (44 inbound and 25 outbound) 
during the PM peak hour (see Table 4). 
Table 4       
Project Trip Generation Estimates 
 
Trip Distribution and Assignment 
The trip distribution pattern for the proposed residential development was estimated based on traffic 
patterns on the surrounding roadway system and the locations of complementary land uses. The peak-
hour trips associated with the project site were added to the roadway network in accordance with the 
distribution pattern discussed above, the roadway network connections, freeway access points, and the 
locations of the project driveway.  
Figure 7 shows the trip distribution pattern and trip assignment at the study intersections. A tabular 
summary of project traffic at each study intersection is contained in Appendix B. 
Roadway Network Under Opening Year Conditions 
The transportation network under opening year conditions (without and with project) is assumed to be 
the same as the roadway network under existing conditions.

4.  
Cumulative Conditions 
This chapter describes the roadway traffic operations under cumulative no project conditions and 
cumulative plus project conditions. The chapter includes the procedures used to determine cumulative 
traffic volumes and a description of the resulting traffic conditions and any adverse effects caused by 
the project.  
Roadway Network under Cumulative Conditions 
The roadway network under cumulative conditions was assumed to be the same as the opening year 
conditions as described in Chapter 3. 
Cumulative Traffic Volumes 
Cumulative traffic volumes were developed using the latest citywide travel demand model, in 
consultation with City’s modeling on-call consultant Kittelson & Associates. Cumulative model volumes 
were developed using 2040 as the horizon year, reflecting the City’s General Plan buildout. As a 
conservative measure, the cumulative condition volumes were assumed to not include the traffic 
associated with the addition of the project. For cumulative plus project traffic volumes, the trips 
generated by the project (see Chapter 3) were added to the cumulative no project traffic volumes to 
yield cumulative plus project traffic volumes. Figure 9 shows volumes under cumulative and cumulative 
plus project conditions. A tabular summary of the cumulative traffic volumes at each study intersection 
is contained in Appendix B.

5.  
Other Transportation Issues 
This chapter presents other transportation issues associated with the project, including: 
• 
Vehicle queuing analysis 
• 
Site access and circulation 
• 
Effects on pedestrians, bicycles, and transit facilities 
• 
Parking 
The analyses in this chapter are based on the City’s Transportation Impact Analysis Guidelines and 
professional judgment in accordance with the standards and methods employed by the traffic 
engineering community.  
Vehicle Queuing Analysis 
The analysis of intersection levels of service was supplemented with a vehicle queuing analysis for left-
turn lanes or stop controlled approaches at intersections where the project would add a substantial 
number of trips. This analysis provides a basis for estimating future storage requirements at the 
intersections under existing, opening year, and cumulative conditions. Vehicle queues were estimated 
using Synchro software. The following movements were evaluated: 
• 
San Mateo Drive and Villa Terrace (Northbound Approach) 
• 
San Mateo Drive and Villa Terrace (Eastbound Approach) 
The Synchro queueing analysis indicates that at the intersection of San Mateo Drive and Villa Terrace, 
the 95th percentile queue would not exceed one vehicle on the northbound or eastbound approach 
under any of the evaluated scenarios. Traffic associated with the project would contribute to a queue 
increase of up to one vehicle at the intersection’s northbound approach. The results of the queueing 
analysis are shown in Table 7.
