Site Access and Circulation 
A review of the project site plan was performed to determine if adequate site access and on-site 
circulation would be provided and to identify any access or circulation issues that should be improved. 
This review is based on the site plan dated November 7, 2025 (see Figure 2 in Chapter 1 and Figure 
10). 
Vehicular Site Access 
Vehicular site access would be provided via a new 20-foot wide full-access driveway to enter the 
garage. The driveway would be on Villa Terrace, approximately 150 feet west of San Mateo Drive.  
Based on the City’s Zoning Code Section 27.64.025, driveways serving three or more parking spaces 
must be minimum 12 feet wide and maximum 20 feet wide. Thus, the proposed 20-foot-wide driveway 
meets the city’s driveway width requirements. 
Traffic Operations at the Project Driveway 
The project is estimated to generate 69 trips (16 inbound and 53 outbound) during the AM peak hour 
and 69 trips (44 inbound and 25 outbound) during the PM peak hour (see Table 4). As shown in Tables 
5 and 6, the driveway will operate at an acceptable level of service under all evaluated scenarios. Less 
than 1 vehicle per minute per direction is expected to utilize the driveway during either peak period 
assuming an even distribution. However, it is likely that there will be instances during which multiple 
vehicles arrive at the driveway at the same time, potentially causing a short queue to form temporarily.  
The site plan indicates that a security gate would be installed at the driveway, approximately 17 feet 
from the sidewalk (see Figure 10). Assuming a vehicle length of 25 feet, it is possible that inbound 
vehicles may temporarily block the sidewalk while waiting for the gate to open. In the event that multiple 
vehicles arrive at the same time, vehicles may need to wait in the street and would temporarily block 
traffic. Storage space at the driveway before the security gate should be lengthened in order to prevent 
this. Given the existing site plan, the security gate should be relocated to approximately 30 feet away 
from the sidewalk.  
Recommendation: The security gate at the driveway should be installed approximately 30 feet from 
the sidewalk in order to minimize the effect of queueing on the sidewalk and traffic operations on Villa 
Terrace.  
Sight Distance at Project Driveway 
The project driveway should be free and clear of any obstructions to provide adequate sight distance, 
thereby ensuring that exiting vehicles can see pedestrians on the sidewalk and vehicles and bicycles 
traveling on Villa Terrace. Providing the appropriate sight distance reduces the likelihood of a collision 
at a driveway and provides drivers with the ability to locate sufficient gaps in traffic and exit a driveway. 
Any landscaping and signage should be located in such a way to ensure an unobstructed view for 
drivers exiting the site. Based on the site plan, trees would be added along the project frontage on Villa 
Terrace. Trees near the driveway should have a high canopy so as to not obstruct the view of drivers. 
The driveway is not set back from the sidewalk and has walls blocking exiting vehicles’ view of 
pedestrians using the sidewalk. A pedestrian warning system should be implemented in order to alert 
pedestrians on the sidewalk of exiting vehicles. 
A minimum of 6 feet of red curb is required on each side of the driveway. The project would provide 6 
feet of red curb to the east of the driveway, and 20 feet to the west, complying with this requirement.  
In the vicinity of the project, Villa Terrace has a slight curve, though this does not affect sight distance.

Recommendation: Appropriate visual and/or audible warning signals should be provided at the project 
driveway to alert pedestrians of vehicles exiting the driveway. 
Recommendation: Landscaping near the driveway should be placed and maintained such that it does 
not interfere with sight distance. Trees should have a high canopy of at least 6 feet and other 
landscaping should be kept at a low level below 3 feet.  
Corner Visibility at Intersection 
The project site fronts the corners of San Mateo Drive’s intersections with Villa Terrace and State 
Street. The intersection corners should be free and clear of any obstructions to optimize corner visibility 
per the City’s standards, ensuring the vehicles approaching the intersection can see other vehicles, 
bicycles, or pedestrians traveling on the cross street. Any landscaping and signage within the safety 
visibility triangle at the intersection corner should be no taller than 3 feet and located in such a way to 
ensure an unobstructed view for drivers on the street.  
The site plan proposes new bulb-outs at the eastern corner of San Mateo Drive and Villa Terrace and 
the southern corner of San Mateo Drive and State Street. The bulb-outs would shorten the crossing 
distances for pedestrians and increase driver visibility at the corners.  
Recommendation: Landscaping provided at corners should be less than 3 feet tall at the corner to 
maintain the required sight distance.  
Vehicular On-Site Circulation 
Within the site, a two-way 24-foot-wide ramp provides access between the ground-level and basement 
parking levels. Each parking level provides only 90-degree parking spaces (see Figure 10). 
Garage Ramp 
City code requires two-way ramps within garages to be designed with gradual slopes and maintain a 
minimum width of 24 feet curb-to-curb and 28 feet wall-to-wall on turns. The site plan includes a ramp 
used to access the below-ground parking level from the ground-level parking level. The ramp has a 
slope of 17.5 percent with 7.5 percent transitions at each end. It has a width of 24 feet curb-to-curb and 
28 feet wall-to-wall on its turn, meeting the City’s requirement for width.  
Drive Aisles 
Based on the City’s standard details for parking, two-directional aisles with standard 90-degree parking 
stalls on both sides should be a minimum of 24 feet wide, while two-directional aisles with compact 90-
degree parking stalls on both sides should be a minimum of 22 feet wide. All proposed drive aisles with 
standard stalls on both sides are 24 feet wide, and the aisle in the basement level with compact stalls 
on both sides is 23 feet wide. The aisles with compact stalls on one side are 22 feet and 9 inches wide. 
Each parking level also includes a drive aisle with no parking on either side measuring 22 feet wide. 
Thus, the drive aisles provided within the garage areas would meet the City’s minimum requirements. 
Parking Stalls 
The proposed dimensions of standard stalls are 18 feet long and 8.5 to 9 feet wide. The proposed 
dimensions of compact stalls are 17 feet long and 8 feet wide. The proposed standard and compact 
parking stalls would meet the City’s minimum requirements. The below-ground parking level also 
includes 4 tandem parking stalls, which would be accessed through the adjacent parking stalls. The 
tandem parking space and adjacent parking should be assigned to one unit. 
Recommendation: Each tandem parking space and adjacent parking should be assigned to one unit. 
Accessible Stalls

--- page 192 ---
715 North San Mateo Drive Residential LTA 
March 5, 2026 
P a g e  |  2 8  
5 ADA parking stalls would be provided on the ground floor parking level per the site plan. Each stall is 
adjacent to an 8-foot-wide access aisle and is 9 feet wide and 18 feet long. All accessible parking stalls 
are near an elevator and an entrance to the building lobby, connected with designated walkways. 
Section 1109A of the California Building Code stipulates that residential parking facilities must provide 
ADA accessible parking stalls at a minimum rate of 2 percent of the covered multifamily dwelling units. 
The project, having 181 dwelling units, must thus provide a minimum of 4 ADA accessible parking 
stalls, with 5 being indicated in the site plan. The proposed number of accessible parking stalls would 
meet the requirement.   
Dead-End Aisles 
On-site vehicle circulation was also evaluated to identify whether there would be dead-end aisles within 
the parking garage (see Figure 10). Dead-end aisles are undesirable because drivers can enter the 
aisle, and upon discovering that there is no available parking, must back out or conduct three-point 
turns. The garage plan shows dead-end aisles at the northeast edges of both garage levels with a 
minimum of 3 feet between the edge of the parking space and the wall. 
Based on the City’s standard details, to provide sufficient area near the end of dead-end aisles for 
vehicles to turn around, there should be a minimum of 3 feet between the edge of the parking space 
and the wall. Thus, the project provides adequate turnaround space at the dead-end aisles per City 
requirements. 
Passenger Loading 
A 25-foot loading zone along the project’s State Street frontage is indicated in the site plan, which could 
be used for passenger loading. The lobby is accessible from this area by a nearby door along State 
Street, and by the main entrance which is connected to the loading zone with a sidewalk. 
Truck Access and Circulation 
The project site plan was reviewed for truck access including delivery and moving trucks, garbage 
trucks, and emergency vehicles, as described below. 
Large trucks and vehicles are not expected to enter the parking garage levels. 
General Loading Operations 
The City of San Mateo requires multi-family residential projects of 50 or more units to provide one 
loading space that is a minimum of 10 feet wide and 25 feet long per City code section 27.64.390.  
The proposed project contains 181 dwelling units and would thus be required to provide one off-street 
loading space that is a minimum of 10 feet wide and 25 feet long. This requirement may be modified by 
the provision of adequate on-street parking along the project frontage that is at least 50 feet from any 
intersections, has convenient access to building entrances, and is wide enough to accommodate 
loading vehicles without impeding the sidewalk or local traffic operation or otherwise be detrimental to 
public safety, as approved by the Zoning Administrator.  
A freight/trash loading space is designated along the project’s frontage on State Street per the site plan. 
The space is 25 feet in length and 8 feet in width and begins approximately 47 feet west of the 
intersection of San Mateo Drive and State Street. The lane width of the loading zone is narrower than 
City’s requirements, however, Public Works has accepted the width of the loading zone to avoid 
encroaching into travel lane. The placement of the loading zone is also less than 50 feet from the 
intersection. The proposed placement has also been accepted by Public Works. 
Garbage Collection Operations

--- page 193 ---
715 North San Mateo Drive Residential LTA 
March 5, 2026 
P a g e  |  2 9  
The site plan indicates a trash room on the north side building on the ground floor. Trash bins would be 
wheeled from the trash room to the loading zone on State Street.  
Emergency Vehicle Access 
Per the 2022 California Fire Code Section D106, multi-family residential projects having more than 100 
dwelling units should have two separate and approved fire apparatus access roads. Where buildings or 
portions of buildings have floors used for human occupancy located more than 30 feet above the 
access road, the minimum unobstructed width is 26 feet for aerial fire apparatus access. At least one of 
the required access roads meeting this requirement should be located within a minimum of 15 feet and 
maximum of 30 feet from the building and parallel to one entire side of the building. All surrounding 
roads provide adequate width and distance for fire apparatus access. 
The project site fronts San Mateo Drive, State Street, and Villa Terrace, which would be used as fire 
apparatus access roads. There is no vehicular access on the west side of the building. 
Pedestrian, Bicycle, and Transit Facility Assessment 
Pedestrian Facilities 
Pedestrian facilities in the study area consist of sidewalks and crosswalks. A complete network of 
sidewalks is present along all of the surrounding streets. Crosswalks with pedestrian signal heads are 
located at all of the signalized intersections in the project vicinity. The project is located between the 
downtown areas of Burlingame and San Mateo, with continuous pedestrian facilities connecting the 
project site to points of interest in each area. 
The project would rebuild the sidewalk along its frontage on State Street, San Mateo Drive, Villa Terra 
removing existing curb cuts on State Street and San Mateo Drive. The new sidewalk would have a 5-foot 
through zone, a 4.5-foot furniture/planting zone, and pedestrian scale lighting, The project would add 
bulb-outs and new curb ramps at the south-west corner of San Mateo Drive and State Street, and at the 
north-west corner of San Mateo Drive and Villa Terrace. The new curb ramps would be built to ADA 
standards. 
Bicycle Facilities 
Bicycle access to the project site is provided via bike lanes on San Mateo Drive. The 2020 Bicycle 
Master Plan identified several bicycle improvements in San Mateo. The plan lists the following facilities 
in the project vicinity as proposed improvements: 
• 
Class IV Separated Bike Lane on Peninsula Avenue between San Mateo Drive and Airport 
Boulevard 
• 
Class II Bike Lane on Peninsula Avenue between Highland Avenue and San Mateo Drive 
• 
Class III Bike Route on Bellevue Boulevard between Delaware Street and Occidental Avenue 
• 
Class III Bike Route on Highland Avenue between Peninsula Avenue and Bellevue Boulevard 
The project provides long-term bicycle storage for the residents in a bike room on the ground floor of 
the project. This room is accessible from a corridor with an entrance on each frontage, including the 
San Mateo Drive frontage, and is thus accessible from the street’s bike lanes. The project would not 
remove any bicycle facilities, nor would it conflict with any adopted plans or policies for new bicycle 
facilities 
Pedestrian and Bicycle Access to Schools  
The project site is located within the San Mateo-Foster City School District and San Mateo Union High 
School District Boundary. San Mateo High School is within 0.5 miles walking distance from the project

--- page 194 ---
715 North San Mateo Drive Residential LTA 
March 5, 2026 
P a g e  |  3 0  
site. It can be accessed via continuous pedestrian facilities along San Mateo Drive and Bellevue 
Avenue, and via Class II bicycle facilities along San Mateo Drive and Poplar Avenue. No public 
elementary or middle schools in the school district containing the project site are located within 0.5 
miles of the project.  
Transit Service 
The project site is serviced by SamTrans routes ECR/397, 46, 53/53P and 292. The nearest bus stop to 
the project site is located at the intersection of San Mateo Drive/California Avenue and Peninsula 
Avenue, approximately 0.3 miles from the project site. The bus stop is served by SamTrans route 292. 
The project site is located within 0.5 miles of the Burlingame Caltrain station. 
It is expected that the project would generate some transit trips to get to the employment areas or to 
other destinations. Based on the 2023 San Mateo County Commuter Survey Results, 15% of 
respondents opted for transit as their mode of transportation, which would result in approximately 11 
new riders during the AM and PM peak hours. The increase in transit ridership could be accommodated 
by the currently available capacity of the bus service as well as the Caltrain service in the area. 
Parking 
Vehicle Parking 
The project proposes to provide 180 vehicle parking spaces, including 5 accessible spaces and 68 
compact stalls.  
California Assembly Bill 2097 (AB 2097) prohibits public agencies from imposing or enforcing any 
minimum vehicular parking requirement on developments located within 0.5 miles of a major transit 
stop as measured with a straight line between any point on any parcels containing the development 
and the nearest edge of any parcels containing the transit stop.1 2 It is important to note that this 
method of measurement is different than the method used to determine the applicability of “close to rail 
transit” trip generation rates, as discussed in Chapter 3.  
A major transit stop is defined as an existing rail or bus rapid transit station, a ferry terminal served by 
either bus or rail service, or a bus stop that is at the intersection of two or more major bus routes with a 
service interval of 20 minutes or less during peak commute periods. The project is located within 0.5 
miles of the Burlingame Caltrain station as measured with a straight line (see Figure 1) and is thus not 
subject to a minimum parking requirement per AB 2097.  
Bicycle Parking 
Per the City’s Zoning Code Section 27.64.262, bicycle parking shall be provided for all new 
development projects.  
 
 
 
 
1 Technical Advisory on the Implementation of AB 2097, Prohibition on Minimum Parking Requirements 
(Statutes of 2022) (California Department of Housing and Community Development, 2025) 
2 AB 2097 Transit Distance Criteria – Letter of Technical Assistance (California Department of Housing 
and Community Development, 2025).

Long-Term Bicycle Parking 
The project would provide long-term bicycle parking in a bike room located on the ground floor. Per City 
Code, the project is required to provide 1 space per studio/one-bedroom unit, 1.25 spaces per two-
bedroom unit, and 1.5 spaces per three-bedroom unit. In total, the project is required to provide 196 
long-term bicycle parking spaces. The project proposes to provide 196 spaces and thus meets the 
requirement. Required and proposed amounts of bicycle parking are shown in Table 8. 
Short-Term Bicycle Parking 
The project would provide short-term bicycle parking along the project frontage on San Mateo Drive. 
Per the City Code, the project is required to provide 0.05 spaces per studio/one-bedroom unit, 0.1 
spaces per two-bedroom unit, and 0.15 spaces per three-bedroom unit. In total, the project is required 
to provide 12 short-term spaces. The project proposes to provide 12 short-term bike parking spaces, 
meeting the City’s requirements.

From: KATHY WEINGAND 
  
Sent: Monday, March 23, 2026 11:18 AM 
To: Joanna Winter <jwinter@cityofsanmateo.org>; sue dreyer 
; 
Stone, Jonathan 
<JStone@prometheusreg.com> 
Subject: 715 /723 N. San Mateo Drive 247 Villa Terrace 
 
March 20, 2026  
   
Dear Joanna Winter, Jonathan Stone, Prometheus Real Estate Group, and Members of the City of 
San Mateo Planning Department and Commission,  
   
We, the undersigned residents of San Mateo Heights, respectfully submit our concerns regarding the 
proposed development at 715/723 North San Mateo Drive and 247 Villa Terrace..  
   
While we recognize the importance of thoughtful development, we believe that the current proposal 
raises several significant issues related to scale, design compatibility, and neighborhood impact. As 
currently planned, the project appears substantially taller and denser than surrounding structures, 
with minimal setback from the sidewalk. We respectfully request that the height of the development 
not exceed that of existing buildings on the west side of North San Mateo Drive, in order to maintain 
consistency with the established neighborhood character.  
   
In addition, the architectural style of the proposal does not reflect the predominantly early-20th-
century character of the neighborhood, which includes Arts and Crafts, Craftsman, Victorian, Spanish, 
and Colonial influences. We encourage consideration of a design approach that is more harmonious 
with these existing styles.

--- page 237 ---
2
We also note the absence of meaningful green space or landscaped areas in the current plans. Given 
that such features are a defining element of the neighborhood, we respectfully request the inclusion 
of park-like landscaping, a community green space, or similar amenities that contribute positively to 
the environment and quality of life.  
   
Setbacks are another important concern. Homes along Villa Terrace and State Street maintain 
consistent front yard setbacks, contributing to the visual cohesion of the neighborhood. We ask that 
the proposed project incorporate a comparable setback—approximately 15 feet—along these streets 
to align with existing development patterns.  
   
With regard to parking and traffic, residents have consistently expressed concerns about existing 
congestion and limited street parking. At the preliminary meeting on February 26, 2025, it was clearly 
communicated that current conditions are already strained. The proposed ratio of 181 residential units 
to 180 parking spaces appears insufficient given typical household vehicle ownership and visitor 
needs. We respectfully request that the project include adequate parking provisions to prevent further 
burden on surrounding streets and residents.  
   
We are also concerned about potential impacts on airflow, sunlight access, and overall quality of life 
for neighboring properties. Appropriate setbacks and design considerations should be incorporated to 
mitigate these effects.  
   
Furthermore, we ask that construction logistics be carefully managed to minimize disruption. 
Specifically, we request that construction vehicles and equipment not be permitted to park on State 
Street or Villa Terrace at any time during the construction period.  
   
In addition, the City Council of San Mateo recently voted to close Villa Terrace and Bellevue Ave. at 
the train tracks which will obviously restrict traffic flow and cause immeasurable congestion 
throughout the entire neighborhood adding another reason why this project needs to be scaled 
back..    
   
We would also like to raise concerns regarding information presented in the project application about 
the property on Villa Terrace (Parcel B). It is our understanding that this property is currently a duplex 
and occupied, contrary to its description as a single-family residence. We respectfully request that all 
project documentation accurately reflect existing conditions to ensure transparency and informed 
decision-making. Also the notice of the Planning Commission public hearing reflects Ross and Diana 
Bowling as property owners giving the insinuation that they are somehow project developers when in 
fact they are not. This affordable housing Duplex will be torn down to make way for these market rate 
unaffordable apartments.   
   
Finally, we believe that new development should contribute positively to the broader community. In 
light of the cumulative impact of development over recent decades, we encourage the inclusion of 
community-oriented amenities such as green space, a garden, or a small recreational area. 
Furthermore, many of us just received notice of the hearing on March 19th for the March 24th hearing 
which is not adequate time for residents to adjust their schedules to attend the hearing.   
   
As a neighborhood, we remain committed to constructive dialogue and collaboration. As long-time 
residents, we expect to be heard, if not by the Prometheus Group, then by the Planning Commission 
of San Mateo,  as we are direct stakeholders and expect that the planning commision advocate for 
us. We provided these comments a years ago and have not seen any change to the project based on 
our comments. We respectfully ask that Prometheus Real Estate Group work with residents and the

--- page 238 ---
3
City to develop a revised proposal that is lower in density, consistent in scale with surrounding 
buildings, architecturally compatible, and inclusive of adequate setbacks, parking, and green space.  
   
Thank you for your time and consideration.  
   
Sincerely, 
Residents of San Mateo Heights  
   
Kathy Weingand

Dear San Mateo Planning Commission,  
 
The California Housing Defense Fund (“CalHDF”) submits the attached public comment re item 1 for 
tonight's Planning Commission hearing, the proposed 181-unit housing development project at 715 N. 
San Mateo Drive, which includes 19 very low-income units. 
 
Sincerely, 
 
James M. Lloyd 
Director of Planning and Investigations 
California Housing Defense Fund

--- page 241 ---
Mar 24, 2026
 
City of San Mateo 
330 W 20th Ave 
San Mateo, CA 94403 
 
By Email: PlanningCommission@cityofsanmateo.org  
 
CC: CityAttorneysOffice@cityofsanmateo.org, clerk@cityofsanmateo.org, 
communitydevelopment@cityofsanmateo.org, citymanager@cityofsanmateo.org; 
jwinter@cityofsanmateo.org  
 
Dear San Mateo Planning Commission,  
 
The California Housing Defense Fund (“CalHDF”) submits this letter to remind the City of its 
obligation to abide by all relevant state laws when evaluating the proposed 181-unit housing 
development project at 715 N. San Mateo Drive, which includes 19 very low-income units. 
These laws include the Housing Accountability Act (“HAA”), the Density Bonus Law (“DBL”), 
and AB 130. 
 
The HAA provides the project legal protections. It requires approval of zoning and general 
plan compliant housing development projects unless findings can be made regarding 
specific, objective, written health and safety hazards. (Gov. Code, § 65589.5, subds. (d), (j).) The 
HAA also bars cities from imposing conditions on the approval of such projects that would 
reduce the project’s density (id. at subd. (j)) or render the project infeasible (id. at subd. (d)), 
unless again, such written findings are made. As a development with at least two-thirds of 
its area devoted to residential uses, the project falls within the HAA’s ambit, and it complies 
with local zoning code and the City’s general plan. Increased density, concessions, and 
waivers that a project is entitled to under the DBL (Gov. Code, § 65915) do not render the 
project noncompliant with the zoning code or general plan, for purposes of the HAA (Gov. 
Code, § 65589.5, subd. (j)(3)). The HAA’s protections therefore apply, and the City may not 
reject the project except based on health and safety standards, as outlined above. 
Furthermore, if the City rejects the project or impairs its feasibility, it must conduct “a 
thorough analysis of the economic, social, and environmental effects of the action.” (Id. at 
subd. (b).)

--- page 242 ---
CalHDF also writes to emphasize that the DBL offers the proposed development certain 
protections. The City must respect these protections. In addition to granting the increase in 
residential units allowed by the DBL, the City must not deny the project the proposed waivers 
and concessions with respect to height, floor area ratio (FAR), setbacks/yards, landscape 
buffers, blank walls, open space, and yard dimensions. If the City wishes to deny requested 
waivers, Government Code section 65915, subdivision (e)(1) requires findings that the 
waivers would have a specific, adverse impact upon health or safety, and for which there is 
no feasible method to satisfactorily mitigate or avoid the specific adverse impact. If the City 
wishes to deny requested concessions, Government Code section 65915, subdivision (d)(1) 
requires findings that the concessions would not result in identifiable and actual cost 
reductions, that the concessions would have a specific, adverse impact on public health or 
safety, or that the concessions are contrary to state or federal law. The City, if it makes any 
such findings, bears the burden of proof. (Gov. Code, § 65915, subd. (d)(4).) Of note, the DBL 
specifically allows for a reduction in required accessory parking in addition to the allowable 
waivers and concessions. (Id. at subd. (p).) Additionally, the California Court of Appeal has 
ruled that when an applicant has requested one or more waivers and/or concessions 
pursuant to the DBL, the City “may not apply any development standard that would 
physically preclude construction of that project as designed, even if the building includes 
‘amenities’ beyond the bare minimum of building components.” (Bankers Hill 150 v. City of 
San Diego (2022) 74 Cal.App.5th 755, 775.) 
 
Furthermore, the project is eligible for a statutory exemption from CEQA pursuant to AB 130 
(Pub. Res. Code, § 21080.66). Caselaw from the California Court of Appeal affirms that local 
governments err, and may be sued, when they improperly refuse to grant a project a CEQA 
exemption or streamlined CEQA review to which it is entitled. (Hilltop Group, Inc. v. County of 
San Diego (2024) 99 Cal.App.5th 890, 911.) 
 
As you are well aware, California remains in the throes of a statewide crisis-level housing 
shortage. New housing such as this is a public benefit: by providing affordable housing, it 
will mitigate the state’s homelessness crisis; it will increase the city’s tax base; it will bring 
new customers to local businesses; and it will reduce displacement of existing residents by 
reducing competition for existing housing. It will also help cut down on 
transportation-related greenhouse gas emissions by providing housing in denser, more 
urban areas, as opposed to farther-flung regions in the state (and out of state). While no one 
project will solve the statewide housing crisis, the proposed development is a step in the 
right direction. CalHDF urges the City to approve it, consistent with its obligations under 
state law. 
 
CalHDF is a 501(c)(3) non-profit corporation whose mission includes advocating for 
increased access to housing for Californians at all income levels, including low-income 
households. You may learn more about CalHDF at www.calhdf.org. 
 
 
2 of 3

--- page 243 ---
Sincerely,

Dylan Casey
CalHDF Executive Director

James M. Lloyd
CalHDF Director of Planning and Investigations

PROJECT BACKGROUND
• Pre-Application
• SB 330 Preliminary Application filed on November 
14, 2024

--- page 258 ---
PROJECT BACKGROUND
• Approx. 258,000 SF Multi-family Residential building
• 181 dwellings
• 19 dwellings to be reserved for very-low-income households (BMR)
• 6 stories / 75’-11” 
• 180 covered parking stalls 
• 131 stalls below grade and 49 on the ground floor
• Access via a new driveway and curb cut to Villa Terrace
• Residential amenities –
• Pool, fitness room & amenity deck on 2nd  floor, common room & 
amenity deck/BBQ area on 6th floor

--- page 261 ---
PROJECT BACKGROUND
• Site Plan & Architectural Review (SPAR)
• New multifamily residential building. 
• Requires Planning Commission approval (building 
within 6-story height limit set by the San Mateo 
General Plan 2040 Land Use Designation of 
Residential Medium II).
• Site Development Permit Application (SDPA)
• Removal of Major Vegetation and Protected Trees. 
• Vesting Tentative Parcel Map (VTM)
• The Project would merge four parcels into one 
parcel. 
• Per SMMC section 26.48.060, the Planning 
Commission is the review authority.

• State Density Bonus Law (Gov’t Code section 65915)

• Unlimited Waivers
• Proposed Project

• 50% Density Increase (60 Units)

General Plan and Zoning Code &

State Law
Affordable Housing
Design Review
Impact Fees
Environmental Review
• Housing Accountability Act (HAA)
• Limits a local agency’s ability to deny, reduce the 
density of, or render housing development projects 
infeasible if objective standards are met
• Housing Crisis Act (Senate Bill 330)
• Project vested – freezes development standards 
and fee structure
• Assembly Bill 130
• New California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
exemption for housing development projects 
• Expedited review process
• Assembly Bill 2097
• Prohibits parking minimums for qualifying projects 
within one-half mile from major public transit stop
State Housing Laws

--- page 267 ---
CODE AND POLICY 
REVIEW
• Projects with 11 or more rental units, must provide 
at least:
• 15% of the units for Lower-Income Households; or
• 10% of the units for Very Low-Income Households
• This project satisfies local BMR requirements by 
providing:
• 15% of the units for Very Low-Income Households.
• The units proposed at the Very Low-Income level 
must also meet local requirements for unit size, 
type, and design.

--- page 284 ---
RECOMMENDED MODIFICATIONS TO 
CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL
Conditions 23, 24 & 92 – “COMPREHENSIVE FEE SCHEDULE”:
Comprehensive Fee Schedule in effect at the time of building permit submittal
Condition 59 – STREETLIGHTS PHOTOMETRICS:
(B) Include a design for lighting all public streets, intersections, sidewalks, pedestrian paths, and
bicycle facilities located in the public roadway right-of-way adjacent to the project site to meet the
lighting levels per the photometric analysis. The analysis shall be based on existing lighting across the
street and any new lighting to be installed fronting the project property.

--- page 285 ---
RECOMMENDED MODIFICATIONS TO 
CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL
Condition 60 – PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS:
(A) SIGNAGE AND STRIPING – Any existing painted curb or pavement markings that were not
removed during the project’s street restoration and are no longer required shall be removed by
grinding if thermoplastic, sand blasting if in paint.
(C) SIDEWALK – The applicant shall replace all sidewalk fronting the project site as shown on the
approved plan set with A.5. Sidewalk Standards – Residential Type C New Development from the
City’s Pedestrian Master Plan.
(D) CURB RAMPS – The applicant shall construct curb ramp(s) in accordance with Caltrans Standard
Plan A88A or other ADA compliant configurations with special approval from Public Works, at N San
Mateo Dr & State St and N San Mateo Dr & Villa Terrace. The actual ramp “Case” shall be identified
on the plans and shall be approved by the Director of Public Works or designee or designee.

--- page 286 ---
RECOMMENDED MODIFICATIONS TO 
CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL
Condition 60 – PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS:
(I) & (J) Replaced with:
STORM WATER CONNECTION – The applicant shall connect to the City storm system using three
connection points at most, where tying directly into the City Storm Main, a wye connection shall be
used in accordance with City Standard Drawings. The applicant shall replace existing catch basin at
the proposed bioretention along Villa Terrace to include overflow drain inlet per approved plans and
in accordance with City Standard Details.
(K) STREETLIGHTING IMPROVEMENTS –
2) Implement associated streetlight infrastructure improvements beyond the project frontage or the
roadway centerline if such improvements are necessary to provide a functioning lighting system for
the project frontage.

--- page 287 ---
RECOMMENDED MODIFICATIONS TO 
CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL
Condition 106 – SITE LIGHTING STANDARDS:
Exterior security lighting in compliance with the Building Security Code “Exterior Security Lighting”
(SMMC section 23.54.060) shall be provided and maintained at all times that the use permitted by this
planning application occupies the premises. Site lighting shall comply with the requirement of an average
illuminance of 1 foot-candle, a minimum illuminance of 0.3 foot-candle, and a uniformity ratio not to
exceed 4:1 average to minimum. Light sources shall be capable of producing a “bright white” light with a
color temperature between 3000K and 4000K and a color rendering index (CRI) of at least 65 unless
otherwise approved. This lighting standard is applicable to all parking lots, driveways, circulation areas,
aisles, passageways, recesses, and grounds contiguous to all buildings. The lighting system shall be so
designed as to limit light spill beyond property lines and to shield the light source from view from off site.

--- page 288 ---
RECOMMENDED MODIFICATIONS TO 
CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL
Condition 108 – PHOTOMETRIC PLAN SUBMITTAL REQUIREMENT:
The building permit plans for the superstructure shall include a photometric plan showing the installation
of lighting fixtures and lighting levels to be reviewed and approved by the Chief of Police or their
designee. The photometric plan shall include point-by-point lighting levels in foot-candles for the entire
plot and ten feet beyond the project property lines. The point-by-point photometric plan shall provide
lighting levels on a grid not to exceed five feet by five feet across the entire site. Each point shall report
the illuminance to the nearest 0.1 foot-candles. Photometric calculations including maximum foot-
candles, average foot-candles, minimum foot-candles, average to minimum uniformity, and maximum to
minimum uniformity shall be included on the plan submitted. Select specifications for fixtures selected
shall be provided on the photometric plan sufficient to ensure compliance with the SITE LIGHTING
STANDARDS.

--- page 298 ---
ARCHITECTURAL PROPOSAL
8
715 N SAN MATEO DR, SAN MATEO, CA  |  PLANNING COMMISSION MEETING   |   MARCH 2026
Design Alignment with City Guidelines:
4.1.2 Articulation Details
•	 2 of 6 facade articulation details are required for mid-
rise buildings   [4.1.2]:
•	 The following 2 details are incorporated into the 
design:
A. Architectural projections such as roof eaves, 
overhangs, cornices, pergolas, or awnings
B. Balconies per unit
C. Box or bay windows per unit
D. Window recesses and edges, including mouldings 
and reveals 
E. Projecting or recessed rooms or units for a 
minimum of 30% of the units for a mid and high-
rise development
F. Horizontal mouldings

--- page 299 ---
ARCHITECTURAL PROPOSAL
9
715 N SAN MATEO DR, SAN MATEO, CA  |  PLANNING COMMISSION MEETING   |   MARCH 2026
Design Alignment with City Guidelines:
4.1.3 Building Materials & Color
•	 To ensure buildings are not monochromatic the 
following strategies are required to be used [4.1.3]:
•	 All 4 requirements are incorporated into the design:
A. A combination of at least 3 different colors and/
or materials but no more than 6 are to be used on 
each building elevation
B. Each color or material shall constitute at least 
10% of the building facade
C. A change in color/material shall be characterized 
by a minimum 6 inch offset from the adjacent 
building plane, or architectural element such as 
moldings or bandings shall be used to create the 
offset
D. Change of materials shall not end at an inside 
corner

--- page 300 ---
ARCHITECTURAL PROPOSAL
10
715 N SAN MATEO DR, SAN MATEO, CA  |  PLANNING COMMISSION MEETING   |   MARCH 2026
Design Alignment with City Guidelines:
4.1.6 Massing Breaks - Mid-Rise Buildings
•	 4 of 9 changes in detailing are required to create 
distinct building segments and add variation to the 
building plane [4.1.6]:
•	 The following 4 elements are incorporated into the 
design: 
i. Change of materials and or colors
ii. Differing window size
iii. Change in window treatments
iv. Inclusion, or change, of cornices
v. Inclusion, or change, of columns or pilasters
vi. Inclusion, or exclusion, of balconies
vii. Inclusion, or change, of horizontal banding  
viii. Wall plane offset a minimum of 18 inches
ix. Change in roof form or heights aligned with the 
building segments

--- page 301 ---
ARCHITECTURAL PROPOSAL
11
715 N SAN MATEO DR, SAN MATEO, CA  |  PLANNING COMMISSION MEETING   |   MARCH 2026
Design Alignment with City Guidelines:
4.1.6 Massing Breaks - Mid-Rise Buildings
•	 At the intersection of two primary streets or a primary 
and a secondary street, building corners shall be 
articulated by incorporating 1 of the following [4.1.6]:
•	 At the intersection of N San Mateo Dr and Villa Terrace 
and the intersection of N San Mateo Dr and State St 
the following element is incorporated into the design:
1. A corner cut at the base of the building
2. A tower element which extends beyond the building 
ridge
3. Special treatment of either different exterior 
materials, paint colors, recesses, or projections 
relative to the adjacent units, or combination of 
these features
4. An architectural element such as a cupola, quoin 
treatment, rooftop sculpture, or spire
